Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauterizations from the roots of Aristolochia (a plant also known as birthwort) in the case of pleurisy. And do it in this manner: take a long root of Aristolochia, the longest and largest that you can find, dry it out, and make it just as thick and long as your arm; and dip it in oil, and then hold it over the fire, and cauterize one cauterization between the ribcage and the collarbone, and two small cauterizations a little lower down in the part that is below the beard; and two cauterizations between the fifth rib and the lowest one, going downwards a little. And one cauterization in the chest, and another on the stomach, and one between the two shoulders, and two at each side of the chest under the cauterization that is between the two shoulders; and do not press your hand tightly, but rather hold it open wide like when smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And ancient men said that someone uses a fire cautery similar to a razor, and they heat it up and place it between the ribs, so long as it comes to that abscess; and the pain springs forth the pus, just as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear for the patient to die now, or a fistula comes that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you cure the disease of the mouse according to what we have said in the division of cures, and it does not benefit, then they apply three manners of cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one manner is that you make three cauterizations, or four, in a line according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the liver cautery that we have said before; and do not press your hand on the whole cautery, and let the patient sit on his back; and another manner of cautery is that you heat the cautery which has two handles, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the key which is at the mouse, or where the patient's wound comes from to the left, and be the elevations by which you lift the key according to the key, according to the length of the body, and the cautery should be according to the breadth of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Then insert the two handles inflamed as much as the key is pierced from the other side, and then remove the cautery, and thus there will be four. And if you wish, then cauterize with all the cautery to three handles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has become too prolonged, and this is better than the other treatments previously mentioned.
de ydropisie	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautionery is not useful for dropsy, except by the manner which is called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help at all, then it is necessary that you make IV cauterizations around the mouth, and I on the stomach, and one on the liver, and I on the spleen, and II behind the back on the spine, and I near the breast; and let the cauterizations be very close to the bone of the skull.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After that, let the cautery stay open for a long time to cause pain, and do not stop the treatment of the patient after the cautery; and then healing will hasten, and both intentions (i.e. the physical and spiritual) will be together with the aid of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cautery for the belly is the trephine (a type of drill or scraper) that we have shown before. And those for the back are olive-shaped, according to what was placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	inflamation of the privy parts (i.e. a condition characterized by swelling in the genital area)
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in the one who is dropsical and are full of clear juice, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the thumb and the ring finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deeply into profundity, thus a fierce awl of citron wood will pierce it, and the cautery should be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that, do two cauteries on each leg, one in each foot at the tip of the little finger. And let the cauteries be long, one under the knee in front and the other behind, in the middle of the leg; and leave the cauteries open for a long time without curing, so that the yellowish fluid comes out. Then cure with the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	From the chamber.
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the affliction of the belly comes from cold and moisture, so much that the vital and digestive forces which are in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by any means of treatment; and you see the patient very suffering and of great virtue, then do I. a large cautery over the stomach according to what it has been spoken of before or the cautery of the stomach, at the cautery circulate; and four small cauterizers around the mouth so that each one is thin like a nail, and two small cauterizers on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, then I do a cautery on the armpit, and one small cautery on each elbow, and two small cauterizers on the stomach near the large one, for the cure is beneficial when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the ulcers are in the fundament, one or more, and are ancient and corrupted by cold and moist humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, but do not profit from it if you make cauterizations: three on the spine of the back, that which is all over under the almacette pouch and pouch in triangulating, and I cautery under the jaw II must; and if you think his stomach is cooled and the food does not cook, and one sees the face swelling, then one makes a great cautery on the stomach, as it is said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cautery pointed; and leave the cautery uncovered for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After healing the place so much as it may be cured.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	It appears to be a medieval medical text, specifically dealing with various treatments for ailments.
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply the cautery to the navel, if it seems necessary, and then put all of it ablaze on that navel-cautered part; and I leave your hand until the cautery comes to the birth of the vein, so that the blood stops; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of navel, cauterize each one as we have said; afterwards treat with salves profitable until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on an ulcer, it will have more aid.
de plaie mal curee	a badly cured wound
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will tell about in its place, this comes to be such a sickness that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When any wound becomes a fistula, and is putrid and flows with foul and corrupt moisture, then you should try to probe it all the way down to its bottom, and know exactly how deep it goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heat the cautery which seems sharp, and put it into the fistula according to the depth that the probe has gone in, and reheat the cautery as long as the corrupt flesh is burnt once, twice, or three times, according to how great a need there is; and beware of burning the nerves that are nearby, and the major blood vessels.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula reaches to the bladder and intestine, then beware of those places, and do not perform this fire treatment on them unless it is in a healthy skin, and think that they are not sinews. After healing the place as much as it may be cured, and if the spot is sealed and the materials have been removed over a long time, then know that the spot is completely healed; and if the materials are not removed, know that the spot is torn and corrupt the bone to its root; and thus as one of those things that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	The sickness of the kidneys.
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the joints and due to great windiness and it does not take a female temperament, then you must make a cautery on the joints from one part and at the same time make a cautery with a clove as we have said before; and if we cauterize them together in the middle, there will be three cauteries in line, and they will become even greater aid.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you make a cautery in the part behind the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and one to the right and one to the left, and each cautery should be as long as the thickness of a finger; and you make one cautery behind the back, or two if you need them; and the cauteries should be clove-shaped according to the form said before.
de la marris	of the kidneys
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidneys are cold and moist, and do not allow conception for that reason, and the flowers are corrupted and their ends are delayed; and when they come, you feel great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauteries around the abdomen, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and two cauteries behind the back; and the cauteries should be clove-shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the groin or hip area
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the moist and viscous substances descend to the thigh of the groin, and because of this cause it moves out of its place, and the signs are that the thigh is longer than the other when you measure them together; and if the seat of the disease is found in the outer area, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the patient above the thigh of the groin with one cautery resembling a circle, and mark before the joint around the thigh as it turns, so that the thigh is inside the circle; and the cauteries should be similar to those used on the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauteries are not available, then make three large olive-sized cauteries on the hipbone, and they should be as deep as all the kidneys; and treat them until they are healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the groin or hip area
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the thigh of the hip, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and the patient is treated with what we have said in the division, and the cure is not worth it, and the disease is ancient: then you must purify the patient with gross humors from fetid pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cautery; and the manner of the cautery is in two ways: that is to say together with burning medicines, and fire cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauterization is in many ways, of which one is such: that you cauterize on the hip bone three triangular cauterizations according to this form, and make them have good depth and great size, and let there be space between each cautery the thickness of a thumb, and they should be olive-shaped; sometimes one makes a cautery in the middle on the head of the hip, for which reason there are four according to this form:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cauterization is at the circular cauterization that we have said before in the dislocation of the hip; but make it in such a manner that the circles contain all the thigh and all the tendons of the joint are burnt.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the manner in which it is done for sciatica, when the pain stays in the hip and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, then one makes two cauterizations there where the patient says that the pain is located, and one cautery above the ankle four thumbs, on the left side a little; and the cauterizations are knife-shaped, and let the thickness of the key be burned inside them; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two fingers from the foot or very near it, then he cauterizes where he feels the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more of them; and if he knows that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, then make a cauterization at the lancet-shaped or circular cauterizer, and be careful with all your cauterizers that you do not burn too little so that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more great harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have seen many who have made a fire cautery on the heel of the foot, and left them so that the leg was completely swollen, and the feet also, and it was pierced and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purge from the belly by which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, make a fire cautery in one and in the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise men said in the case of the hip cautery, of what this is the manner: make such an iron and let it be at the head as thick as a walnut shell or a little less, and let there be between the parts and from one part to the other the length of a nut's breadth; and let the parts between be two-thirds [long], and also like nuts, and you have a hip irons well made; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be heated until it is entirely red and smells of sulfur, and then put it on the wooden stump of the sick hunchback, and turned on the healthy side; and cauterize once .i. cautery repeated and leave alone for three days; and then make a poultice with butter, and let the wound remain open for a long time; after the cure with ointment until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use a poultice of this cauterization for the fear of his gaze, and see if we are among those who use it; and however these are good cauterizations, which can bear it, and the place where it applies.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The medical cautery of fire is such that you make the instrument to be between two things in which the margin of the door descends, and it is made of brass or iron with a long handle, and on top has II nails, and has space between each one the size of a thumb; and they should be open at the front and back, and join together as in this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	Put on the buttock of the patient lying on his side with a cloth spread out beside him, and put your hand close to the buttock; after that pour between the two circles of hot oil which has been heated in the fire one pot, and let it be for one hour short of time, and suffer the patient to feel the heat and burn.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it finds similar mordication as fire; and when the mordications have passed, lift your hand with the instrument and raise the hot buttock off of the patient, and let it be thus for three days, and put on butter so that what is black from the scorching may be removed; and leave it for three days until the ulceration goes away; and this would be the last aid after the cure of ointments as long as he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has extended to the thigh or down to the leg, make me a tool that takes away according to what you have done in the same way; and this is the method of taking away hot water, and I have written it in the treatise on the correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkaline and live charcoal, as much of one as of the other, and crush them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Where there is a small hole at the bottom so that the point of a dagger can enter; and place above it another pot well weighted down, and place on top alkaline and charcoal and sweet dew on top, until there is enough above the powder to have you grasped it with your hand; and let it be thus until it makes hot water and vinegar or the weighted-down pot boils, then take all that hot water, and pour it on top of charcoal and alkali just as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very painful and should be administered in various works of medicine and cauteries of other members For it does great harm like fire, and also other medicines which are cauterized well on the skin such as theriac, and honeyed anacardium and calamus with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment by which one man was cured of the pain in his side and sciatic vein, and greatly praised it, and says that no other treatment was done to him, and he was healed at once when this treatment was made, and he had bathed himself as it teaches here below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same manner that you take green verdigris fresh and dry, and grind it well with a pound of fat, and put it on the side and thigh and leg where the pain is, and bind it; and let him be for three hours and by the quantity that the patient does not feel the burning anymore.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter into a bath so that his body is well warmed up, and put him to bed, and the pain will go away altogether and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use cauterization of such medicine, unless after the evacuation of body.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with a fire made from goat hair, it helps much; and the cautery should be done in such a manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and grease it with old oil, and put it on the hollow between the thumb of the foot and the other which is called heel.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take dry goat hair, and put it to the fire so that it is carbonized, and put it on the linen, and let it be until it cools down; and do it again in this way, and cease not from doing thus until you think by sense that it comes up to the thigh, and that the pain ceases; and this manner of cauterizing is called "cautery of goat hair".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either by falling or by percussion or by too great evacuation, or by appearances of cold material spread out, none of these appearances is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from the infestation of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after these that the sick person be freed of fetid pills or other appearances, and that one make on the back, there where the pain holds, three lines marked with ink, and in each line five cauterizations or more according to the virtue and quantity that the sick person can bear; and let the cauterization be done according to the cauterization which is called "poins"; and if you see it, make 3 cauterizations or 4 at the middle of the clavicle in this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have narrow hips when they tie up, and pain; and you find in the last spine of the back and on the nape, the appearance that comes over the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it curing, then cauterize at the cauterization of poins according to this form:
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery shall penetrate evenly each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that, then you shall cauterize around the spine with fire cautery, at two or three lines, and the points shall be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, let the place be soothed until it is sound according to what we have said, and be careful that you do not introduce fire cautery into a swelling which is near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain of the joints is due to swelling in all members of the body, and when the pain comes in feet, which doctors call "podagre" properly, and when it is from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauteries in this manner: make many cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-sized according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then let the fire cautery reach all the way to the point that one calls "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come just to the knee and at other joints, and such things happen many times, then let fire cautery be applied on each knee three or four cauteries or more of each part, all the way to the olive-shaped part; and if you need even more, do that, but do not hold your hand too long until the splinter of the cautery stick is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and to the back, administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the knuckle II lines; and if there remains no pain in them, make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pains come to just below the ribs or just to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good government over the patient and administer medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make good government and purge phlegm, it will be made healthy by the aid of God.
de la routure dou syfac	Of the inflammation of the spleen
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the swelling comes on suddenly, and the bowels descend to the groin and it is new, you must not let him be cured that day; and have him do things that loosen his belly, so that the filth descends from his belly; after make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to stretch out his leg as long as the swelling is repaired, and sew them up at your fingers, and then give him an incision below the dislocation over the bone of the elbow, and draw it up in a sign that resembles half a circle above the body; then heat the cauterizing instrument whose shape:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he is white and emits fetid discharges.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the intestines to their place; and the attendants wash his hand over it so that they do not return back; and work well on the patient's thighs, and put a cushion under him and a servant above the thighs, and another above the chest who holds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign in your entire hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, start again another time until you reach the bone; and be careful subtly that the intestines do not burst when you do the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that through this the patient does not die, or become worse.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come just to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to their measure, and for grown men also as large as their measure; after 3 days cure the place of the cautery with butter as long as the scabbing is removed; afterwards cure other ointments until they are healed, and let the patient lie on his back for 40 days so that the wound is well closed; and it is necessary that these swellings be lanced for a long time, so that the boils do not burst when he will get up to go into bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, have him wrapped in a well-made bandage and leave it on for another 40 days; and have good rest, that he does not stir too much and beware of excessive drinking and eating, and of loud breathing; and when he does this instruction then he is entirely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say after this the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the hernia of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come into other parts of the body and are recognized, and you see that they no longer grow, then make a cautery on the cautery again according to its quantity, and let it be red the third part from the cure; after the cure according to what we have said; and none of the ancients have said that one must cauterize with a cautery at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the navel and make a line across it over the ulcer, and another one below, and with your hands on both sides fill up the whole cauterized area.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more superficial.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of ancient pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any member, either from falling or being hurt, and that pain lasts a long time, and the cure of medicine does not help, then it is necessary that it be cauterized with the cautery which is called "poins", and let the cauteries be according to the length of the member and its smallness and weakness and virtue and location of twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is clean from the first cautery, that's fine; if not, repeat the other cautery on him, because it is a custom that it must move to the member that is nearest to it, so you should do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	It seems like we've reached the end of a medical text written in an old language, likely Middle French or Old French.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The swellings are aided sometimes by a cautery with great help, and indeed the sickness that comes from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see it being cauterized, take care if the sickness is at the beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not decline or stay, and you doubt that the corruption will spread throughout the patient, then make five cauterizations on the head: I inside the head right away, and the other towards the forehead at the end of the eyebrows; and II on the two horns, and I behind on the nape; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches just to the bone, and until the scabs come out from which the vapors of thick humors can issue; and cauterize on the mule according to what is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the swelling is spread throughout and it is clearly evident, then it is necessary that you do the cauterizes of these five cauters on the head, and one cautere in front of the navel, and two cauters on the spine of the neck, and six cauters on the spine of the back, and one large on the croup and another nearby, and two on each shoulder; and two on the ribs, and two on the tendons of the breast, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the palms of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are on the rear of the calf, that you do not burn them; and sometimes make a cautere on the bone of the fistula, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	Know that the more I do of a cauterization, the more it aids you and benefits you; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cauterization if the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterizations be great and small according to the members and joints, as you will find in manners of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterward treat with flour of wheat several times with honey and other treatments until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a swelling comes on any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauterizations on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be a point entering into the depth of the flesh; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at any time one makes a cautery and to the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is removed the inflammation; and nonetheless no one interferes with it unless they are knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	of swellings
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is inflamed, and the cause of medicine is of no use, then cauterize it with a cautery a pea deep, according to the quantity of the white of the skin, until the swelling is removed, and its color is changed; then cure it with flour of vetches and lentils with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood of hen and blood of goose, each one in part; and mix everything together, and tie it up with a cloth, and air it at the level until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for chancre by cauterization
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a cancer comes at the beginning, and you see it arresting, then cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the edge of the cancer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nonetheless the wise men said that one should also cauterize in the middle of the cancer; and nonetheless this does not seem good to me, because I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it come about once; and a more direct thing is that it be cauterized around, with the cautery called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some person has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in dying or because of the superfluity that it makes or because the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has a lot of blood, or because of the swelling; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize it with a lot of small cauters all around where it hurts; afterwards leave him so.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it perforate through the entire cautery, then heat the cautery with which it is made.
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the midst of that illness called "adubelati" as long as the cauters have pierced the skin, and be such cauters that the patient feels them everywhere in this manner that the course of the ulceration is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards heal him until he is perfectly cured.
li cure dou feu par fer	the treatment with fire by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of illness is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a gangrene of the member, for it gnaws the members just as fire gnaws on dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this illness in a place that can suffer a cautery together with fire, then heat up the cauterizers, small and large, according to what is needed at the place where the illness is; afterwards, cauterize all around until you eradicate all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted be removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the places that have been cauterized a poultice with oil until the scalds from fire are removed, and all the corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ointments produces pus.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy pus does not form, it is good; and if so, repeat the cauterization on those parts which remain from the corrupted places.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ointment has at some time been cured with hot water in place of a fire cauterization; but nonetheless fire cauterization is more great help, and I have already said the cure of hot water in the division: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Des pores that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often happens that on feet for a long time there grows a disease which is called "clod" according to our intention, and it is a thick growth that hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cautery of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say fire cautery and hot iron cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat the iron like a pen made of copper, and it should be made from good iron to its length so that it can penetrate the growth from all sides, and have fine edges; then put it hot on the growth and turn your hand completely around the growth until it reaches the point of the growth; and let it be thus for three days until it begins to rot; then make a poultice of bitter wild rue crushed with oil, and leave the poultice on all night, and the growth will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with ointment applying fat until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if it is converted into pus from the body, and often occurs in hands and feet, then you must apply a hot iron cautery; and do thus: take a lead or iron rod, or a wooden splinter, and put on the lump and the abscess, that is to say the little warts called porles verrues; and put the rod on so that it can surround everything, then put in a bit of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edge of the rod comes to the root of the lump, and let the hot water penetrate deeply enough to reach the root; and let the patient bear the burning of the hot water for an hour; then leave it like that, and it will come out with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do as with another, until you remove all those that are within the body, then treat them of ointments which bring forth flesh.
li cure dou trembler	I see a shift to a new topic!
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some person trembles with cold or quartan fever or another illness, it is necessary that you make four cauterizations or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one on the hip, and one above the stomach at the olive cautery; then let him shake out and hasten to recover from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of blisters bursting
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes appear on the outside of the body blisters, or suppurating pustules, that come from thick corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	Then it is necessary at first when they appear that one makes a cauterization on the head of each pustule: a subtle cautery of mulberry wood, whose tip is seized by fire, or of a long root of aristolochia, or a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes when one cauterizes them at the beginning when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow further ahead, but the superfluities from which they come are ruptured and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great outpourings of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that appears on the surface, or at the incision of the aposteme, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to staunch.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And nevertheless, when these things happen to anyone, if you hasten to put your two fingers on top of the wound where the bleeding is coming from, and press as hard as the blood is stilled under your fingers, and no more drips come out; then heat up several small and large olive cauteries in the fire until they are all red; then take one, either a big or small one depending on the size of the wound and the location where the artery is exposed, and place it on that vein while you hold your fingers on top of the wound, and keep the cautery there until the bleeding is stemmed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts forth again when you lift your fingers from the wound, and the cautery cools down, then take another one quickly from those that are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing these things one after the other until the bleeding is stemmed; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other mischief comes upon the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well stopped right away itself, especially if the artery is large, unless it is done by one of the four methods we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not tied up, or by tightly tying a thread, or by applying medicines that have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be tied and compressed properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who would remind me of the futility of stemming bleeding by tightly tying a cord or by applying hot things on top, or similar things, if they do not help at all. (Note: This seems to be a reflection on the fact that some methods mentioned earlier are not effective in stopping bleeding from an artery)
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and he does not have a surgeon or medicine present, then he should put his two fingers on top of the wound as we said, and press well until it is stemmed over the wound and vein; and do not move his fingers, but rather moisten them with cold water often as long as it is very cold so that the blood congeals and thickens and stops bleeding; and make inquiries ahead to get what he needs in terms of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on surgical remedies.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all diseases into which fire must be applied, or hot medicine, and reasons, and causes, and instruments, and forms of cauterization; and I placed that chapter at the head to the end of this book, and I will go through this chapter by the same route so that what you want is found more easily.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And therefore that I begin this, you, dear child, must learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterization, and for that it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the operation of this chapter there has been many times evacuation of blood when opening the vein, and incising above the abscess, and treating wounds, and extracting splinters, and incising on the bone, and similar things; or else death occurs to more than one.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to undertake folly.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many types of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	if they come with such a condition that they die easily because of the foolishness they find in their illness, and the great severity of their wickedness; and from these one should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are some who give you their opinion, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the sickness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is not necessary that you consent to those who come to you with this manner, but place more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not act foolishly but wisely of those from whom you are certain, and of whom you can take and have profit; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients for whose salvation may be converted; and these will help you to achieve good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, may Our Lord give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to aspire to the holy inspiration of His hand, Amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Now I have ordered this chapter for you in dividing it by chapters, as is before the chapter on cauterization, which I divided from top to bottom for you, so that you may find more easily what you will need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	A double basin full of water. (This phrase appears to be a heading or title in the text, possibly indicating that this section deals with surgical procedures involving water.)
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease often comes to children at birth, and when the cord is too tight around the child's head. And sometimes it comes from a cause unknown, or unexplained.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease occur in anyone except children, and of all the ones I've seen it was the death that hastened. And because of this, it seems to me that I am not justified in wasting my work on such cases.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I have seen a child whose eyes were full of water and the head was swelling every day so much that it could no longer be supported; and it seemed to me that he would die, and this swelling is assembled beneath the bone above the orbit, between the eye and the bone. And the operation is such that if the swelling is between the eye and the bone, and the abscess is small, you make a cut in the head as wide as two thumbs, so long as the swelling runs; and see here the shape of the spatula:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is more swollen, and the abscess is larger, make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is under the bone, and you see signs that the corners of the head are open on each part, and the point jumps up when you press it with your hand from the inside, and this has not been resolved: then you must make three incisions in the head according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, draw out all the moisture entirely.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After secure the slits of cloth and powder, and I put wine and oil in them, and leave thus until the fifth day; then loosen it, and treat the wound with tents and ointments, and let the head be strained equally, and give food to the patient dry meat without moisture until the member is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another manner of incision is that you look where the prominence of the abscess opens and the point of the pus gathers; for it may be in front, or behind, or to the right, or to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut the spot where the abscess opens and the gathering of pus is located, and make the incision as far as you can; and be careful not to cut into the artery, lest there flow a flood of blood, so that the patient dies from the loss of blood and the evacuation of moisture.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the deafening of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.
