de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the deafening of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a perforation in their ears; and the same thing happens to men through deafening of a wound or a boil inside the ear, and this deafness sometimes goes deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is one little hole left after the perforation, and the voice sounds muffled.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	So then the one that goes deep, if it can't be seen, is due to severe inflammation in several dispositions, and the one that can be seen comes from putting the sick person's ear into the sun; and look inside: if you see a whitish congealment, then this operation has all its proper shape.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be cut and scraped before and behind all smooth, if it does not hurt the ear; if the congealment is from pus or core of the ear, then take fine tweezers and gently pick it out, until that pus is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the stoppage is very deep in the ear, take the sharp thin razor and heat it a little over the fire, then put it into the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you sense the inflammation from which the patient feels pain in the ear, pierce lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then put into the ear a tent according to the width of the perforation, and anoint with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is healed, or take a tent and moisten it in rosewater, and powder on vitriol powder; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is necessary to remove the tent and put another tent soaked in cerote made of rose oil and wax, so that the swelling may be removed; and then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding continues to come out, then dip a sponge and wrap it in cold water, and put it on the ear, and make use of other remedies that remove the bleeding from the wounds, such as treating with decoctions and distillations.
de la char des papieres	It seems like you've added a few lines from an old medical text.
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	The following althelul that come from papers of the eyes when they are moist and are dry, you should stretch them with tweezers and pincers, and cut off a spatula from its roots; then put on the place vitriol powder.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if it does not peel off, then cauterize with a subtle lenticular cautery, and the cauterizer after incision is worth moving; and many times repair, since nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are charred and do not return.
de la gresle	hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come into the eyes small things that seem like frost in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture above and below the paper; the procedures are such: watch if the grandine moves from one part to another, and it is a light thing to know; then make it broad, then scrape off each part lightly, then take it with forceps, and cut.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot cut it without piercing a little the paper, then do not harm anything to the patient; and if the tear is large, assemble it with a suture, and cure until it be sound; and if it is small, do no force, for the ointments will heal it quickly and make good flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the granule is descending inside the ear towards the top part, turn the paper over and take the granule with pincers, cut it and press from one side to the other; and if the paper is pulled away by the incision, it doesn't harm anything; and when the granule has been cut, wash out the eye with salt water, and cure the place where it left a mark until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	meibomian gland cyst or chalazion (a type of eyelid lump)
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is drained onto pieces of paper above, and this occurs more in children than in anyone else, and it causes them great pain to their eyes, and they come with the catharrhe in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears rush to their eyes; and for that reason they lie on their faces at once, and sleep on them, and their papers are below their eyelids moistened by the inflammation and appearance which have covered the exinach appearing in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the place to your two fists and feel the exinach between them.

And the way to do it is that the patient places their head in your lap. Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Take then a whole piece of linen cloth and stretch it between your two fingers from the front; and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to press on the cut, that you do not bruise all the surrounding tissue up to the eye, that you do not blind it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the skin does not open at the beginning of the cut, then stretch the cut slightly so that it opens; then pull it out as we have said, then wet linen cloths in ale and water, and place them on the wound, and then strain to bind.

Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hot abscess comes to the place, then heal with soothing plasters until it is sound.
des poilz des papieres	of papers of wool
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When papers grow hairs that are grafted on to them and are inflamed, they harm themselves and cause various kinds of diseases such as habitual tears and moistening of the papers and albugine, so long as it is a cause of destruction of themselves; and the cure is according to four manners: or by cauterization with fire together, or by medicinal water according to what is before in the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and suturing or by catheters, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you place the patient's head in your hands, then turn the paper from the eye to your left hand; if it has turned, it's good; if not, put a needle with one thread above it and insert it into all of the grafted hairs on the edge of the paper where the hairs have grown. Then pull out the thread and place a small patch of cotton and linen under the paper in the area of the grafted hairs, covering the entire space from the large tear to the small one. Then take out the thread and sew above the paper a figure of lint, like the leaf of myrtle, and always it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you see the paper swelling up.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if you have someone who needs it, take a large quantity of paper, according to how the paper is moistened; then do on the entire spatula above the two lines that you marked, and start with a great tear right up until it's small; and let one of the incisions be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the thread into one of the two angles that are curved, then scrape off all of it; then join the two lips to a stitch with a needle on very fine woolen thread, and wipe away the blood, and make dry the superfluity of threads above the two wicks in any gluey things you see doing this; and if not, don't bother, then leave the stitches and threads until three days or four; then heal the wound without stitches from drying and compressing things, for the paper revives at the joining of the wound and assembly, but the stitch is dead (as the ancients said), and it's a task without fear; and there is another way: which is that you mark the paper with a figure that is like the shape of myrtle leaves, as we have recounted, to three loose threads according to the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take note of what rises to equal strength simultaneously according to the shape which is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you do not have the strength to hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with some thread on it, and put it in the shape; and put one end of the thread near the large lip, and the other end near the small one, and assemble between your fingers the threads equally; then lift your hand equally, and lift up all the skin over which you have marked, as we have recounted, then assemble the two lips of the wound by suturing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with wax and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hair of the paper is converted: so it behooves you to use what we have said about the incision; but the suture in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds in the tail is as follows: and it is that you convert the paper and make a hole inside according to what I have said, and then make two stitches by art, and two thin strings also long as the length of the paper and the width of the space between them; and take hold of the two ends of the threads on each side; then assemble one and the other carefully above what rises from the oil paper, and strain out the two stitches from both parts together; and let it be thus for some days, and the skin that is strained will die and become black and wither, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the skin closes with sufficient strength, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has been sewn up, and the paper has been lifted off, and the hairs will no longer be felt; and this is the shape of the two suture lines that you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedure is as follows: take a thin needle, and insert one thread of fine silk into it; then take the two ends and tie them together carefully, making sure the length of the threads is about a palm's width. Then, place another thin thread of silk alongside the first one, and tie the end of the thread. Put the patient's head on the thread, and let it be in the sun so that the procedure is clarified, as this is a delicate and small procedure. Insert the needle into the root of the hair closest to the paper, and make a hole quickly until you can draw it out above the natural hair. Then, pull out the natural hair with the thread attached to it, if there is one or two or three or more hairs; then pull your hand gently until all the hairs come out together with the thread in the paper.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the thread is pulled out and the hairs do not come with it, you will pull the thread underneath all the thread that you have placed, until the thread comes out from above through the small hole and you can see it with your eyes. Then, once you have pulled out the thread and the hair, close the eye and let it be closed for two or three days, until the hair settles in its place and a new skin grows over it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the inflammation of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this illness called "aleacrati" or the ulceration comes to the eye, there are two manners in which it occurs: the one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it occurs through sudden injury, or cutting, or cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treating it is that you cut open the wound, and separate the lips of the eye, and put linen tents in it, and bind it until it heals; and it does not seem right to use in its treatment things that dry up and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the illness will come back worse than it was at first; but there is work with things that soften and moisten, such as fenugreek; and rose of water or aloes and flax seed cooked, and ointments made from aquilona melted in some oil, and I would enfold a tent, and treat with these.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you keep watch so that it does not heal in the same form as before; and these operations which we have said are nothing other than precautions against this disease, so that it does not return in the same form as before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	Of the flesh (or ulcer) that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is located below, which is truly called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cauteries and similar things; and the way of working in this is that you take a needle with it having two threads, and stick it into the flesh, and make it pierce from the left armpit to the right, so that the thread comes out at both joints of the flesh; then bind the skin above up to all the needle, and sew with a large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper comes back according to what is needed, it's good; if not, take a razor and put it in the cut, and turn the paper, and make two cuts or sides within the paper; and be the joints of the two cuts at the two angles of the incision that you sewed up, and make an angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is as the shape of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove that skin, according to the quantity that its edges are worn out beneath, from what follows the paper; then join the two severed parts, and sew with a thread of linen; then do the cure of what we have said of soothing medicines, and bandages, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from an incision or cut or burn, it is fitting that you make a straight incision underneath the layers of paper, and according to what has been said before; then separate between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said. And the operation should be done in accordance with the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form. The wise masters prepare an instrument from all their power so that they can make the figure return to its natural shape. And the patients themselves, according to what is fitting for treatment and instruments, and in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the suddenness of paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this wound has in many men in the same manner that the paper above is stuck with the white of egg, and cannot move or do its natural activities, then it is necessary for you to put the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and let it be so fine, not too sharp nor too cutaneous, that the patient cannot suffer if the saw blade cuts into the eye; and your incision, from which you scrape off this assembly, should be light, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and the entire assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye a salted water is applied, and a sweet wine is lifted up, and a cordial; then put between the paper and the eye a linen cloth, and place on the eye wool soaked in egg white; and after the third day use of the cordial and other similar things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	the corner of the eyelid
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It is known that the corner of the eyelid is in two ways: it is nerve-like and resembles a hard yellowish scab, and another which is not nerve-like, but rather resembles frozen white moisture, so that when one touches it with iron and tries to pierce it with needles, it cannot be pierced; and both appearances begin towards the large tear sac, and grow little by little until it covers all the eye and its light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	The method of incision is as follows: the patient puts their head in your hand, then opens their eyes; and you take the paper with your hand, then pierce the corner of the eyelid with needles of small thickness, upwards. Then take a needle, and put one hair from a horse, cow, or ox, and a strong thread on it; and double the point of the needle slightly, and insert it into the corner of the eyelid, and perforate it through the entire needle, and tie the corner of the eyelid with a thread and stretch it upwards. Then scrape off all the hair from the side of the eyelid that touches the tear sac and the glue to the hair just up to the tip; then cut the remaining part in the root of the tear sac with a very fine sawing motion and small forces, and leave the natural flesh of the tear sac so that the body's tears do not come through the incision as usual. And sometimes tie the corner of the eyelid only with the onion and thread, as we have said; then scrape off all the soft tissue from this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the tissue does not touch the cartilaginous membrane and break it, and that the tear sac is not pierced. And after the incision, pour a little bit of burnt silk thread into the eye, and made from litharge, and let it stay until the next day; then cure it with whatever is necessary until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not numb, and you cannot insert the needle, and the splinter cannot enter, this kind of nail condition is often treated with medicine; and it appears like I have described in the section, and if you see it covering, then work on the eye of the patient, and take a small piece of light spatula according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And reset the nail above gently, and if you see that it does not decrease at all and the pain increases, then spit into the eye a cord made of litargyria and red sulfur and it will congeal, and stop the eye until the next day; then continue with the other work according to this same action, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If anything is not contrary in the eye, as a hot apostema or boil, then drain it, and first cure the hot apostema until it is healed, then continue with the work just as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid harms in the eye by great damage, then suspend it with the needle, and cut a part of it but not all, so that the body of tears does not come; then spit into the eye red collier made of litargyria.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	It seems you've changed to a new topic.

des voines des eulz	of veins of eyes
