de la fistule de l’oil	It seems that the text has come to an end with "de la fistule de l'oil", which means "of the eye abscess" or "fistula of the eye". This is likely a medical term from the Middle Ages, referring to a condition where there is an abnormal connection or channel between the inside and outside of the eye.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Li mire (a surgeon) call it "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cautery and with hot medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is an artifice in it that you must cut on top of the abscess, where it should die, and drain out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered and you see the corruption and blackness, then take out all the instrument that has been there, and this is the form of the "aspre chief", which is a tool used for this purpose. And it should be made of iron with a pointed end like a file, and should be pointed in the same shape as it is shown here:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it on the corroded bone, then turn it between your hands and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption has been removed. And do this several times, then restore the site with medicinal cauterizations.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	if the swelling is hardened, and flesh grows there, and the head of the boil is hardened, and remains so for XL days, and it does not break out again and is not abscessed, and a bad accident does not occur, know that he is healed; if not, then there is no other cause than to bring the fistula back into the navel according to this shape: and this is that you uncover from the bone the second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it has been uncovered so take a needle according to this shape, and be the iron needle at III angles, and the shaft is thinned down as far as the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it on the bone beside the swelling, and move your hand away from the eye I point to. Then turn all the way with the force so that it penetrates the bone and the patient will feel it as the vein swells if you keep your hand on their neck; and then restore the joint with dry medicine, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh grows and hardens around the place, let the matter go to the neck; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of the eye (i.e. the pus or fluid)
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the issue of the eye is completely open and does not come out through the nape or a decrease, you should bind the patient; then dress it, then put on a poultice with hot iron to bleed, then put on the eye, i.e. the compress made from aloe and encens and sarcocolle and linen; and then strain the eye, and fill it up with bandages and cloths; and the manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and double each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the issue needs; then strain it by a strong cloth above, and repeat the poultice to bleed without pain; then remove the poultice and leave the eye strained day and night, and if the compress becomes wet, you should bind it tightly; then remove the compress after a day and a night, and if you see the eye repairing itself, it is well; if not, you should repeat the dressing and the cloths and the compress and the poultice until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Of the rupture of a transparent membrane (i.e. a detached retina)
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the rupture comes in the transparent membrane (i.e. a retinal detachment), then it opens and comes out through the papillae like a grain of resin, and it is frightening to see; then if you see it happen, the treatment is as follows: you put an needle into the root of the part below up to that above, then put another needle where there is a double thread from the margin; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle in its place; then cut the end of the double thread and tie a part of the membrane around it, and strain it well, then extract the needle and put on the eye a linen cloth moistened with egg white; and let it be until the thread sticks with the membrane, then cure the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed; and at any time the wound is strained by the membrane each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eye has a great appearance (i.e. severe inflammation), then pierce it with a fine needle that comes in from the center of the eye, and scrape away the yellowish moist part (i.e. the cornea) and descend into the eye itself; then pull out the needle as soon as possible, and strain the eye until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	Of the lower part of the eye (i.e. the conjunctiva or the sclera).
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing other than the bowstring that is assembled in the eye, resembling water flowing down, and it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then take their head between your hands from two parts, and pull out so much as to see the string come up to your eyes; then stop and do not let it descend and clear the light, and see the things with the patient as he normally does; and if it does not descend below, know that it is a vein, and if the descending of the string is not arranged as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Have the patient sit between your hands; then take the fine spatula and place it on the hardened tissue I call the "poc" by the continuation of the conjunctive with the hardened tissue and the crown, until the fluid is released; and when it has been issued, have it distilled into the eye in hot water mixed with honey, or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and honeyed; then be cured with another cure until she is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	Of the threads (i.e. filaments) of the eye.
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the likenesses of water in divisions and that which is needed to pierce; do work accordingly for healing.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You must have the patient sit between your crossed hands, outside of the light for the sun, and close the healthy eye tightly; then put the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eye is on the left, or in your right hand if the eye is on the right; then take in your right hand if the eye is on the left, or in your left hand if the eye is on the right, the instrument called "almagda"; then place the point of the instrument near the crown through a thickness of a reed into that white part of the eye up to the smaller lachrymator; then push the instrument called "almagda" firmly and turn your hand until it penetrates in the white part of the eye, and feel when almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be at the depth of the measure of the length from the pulp up to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the eye; if you see bone in that paper through the clearness of the hardened tissue, then put the instrument next to where the water is, then press under one way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he has water now, so sees the patient before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	Afterwards rest for a short time, and if the water rises again the second way, put force with the instrument, and when it is well set and does not rise, then draw out gently by turning your hand little by little; and then dip in water a piece of new thread, and wipe from that the eye inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put behind the eye a poultice or wet cloth in rose oil and abundance of egg white, and bind with clean linen.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We now, and those who are of our time, put on a compress with abundance of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almond cannot enter into the eye by its hardness, for there are many men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument which is called "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And then puncture the conjunctiva alone, and do not go too deep, but make it subtle, then put in alum, as we have said; and on completing the work prepare for the patient a bed fittingly, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and be careful of all movements, and give him light food, and do not move his head nor to the right nor to the left, and keep him bound according to his disposition until the third day; then loosen it in the same dark house, and inspect his sight, and make him look at some things, and then put back the bandage until the seventh day; and you must not do this in the heat of the cure or after the incision now, but rather speed up these things, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess forms, you shall loosen the eye on the seventh day in front of it, and direct the instrument that soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, then loosen the view and put a covering on its face to cover any day, and be instantly in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then the house becomes small and small, and it turns into its case; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Yrach, who said that in his peaceful land they made someone insert almond into the eye, so that they could draw out the water, but nonetheless I never saw anyone doing this in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the shapes of almond forms, because those who do not know them see them as such, and they are made of pure gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads should be the same subtle shape, and the base in three sharp points.
de la char sor le neis	from the skin above the navel
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	At times births or newborns are born with various conjoined limbs, of which some seem like scorpions to many feet; and if they have such with a limb twisted in a foul color, and if it has a soft skin of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore of those limbs that are soft and not twisted, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the ointment on those limbs, and burn them; then seize what you can grasp with the sharp instrument from one part, until you know that all that limb is loosened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that you cannot cut out, open it all up with thin, sharp instruments; until nothing is left. If the abscess bursts on its own, or opens without your doing anything to it, then let it heal itself, and the scabs will come off as they should. And if it's malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize them until the pain is extinguished, and all the flesh lumps are cut out; then pour vinegar or wine into it.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the needle works and moisture comes just to the palace, know that he is healed; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is dead flesh in the bone above, to which instruments do not come to cut: then you must put a thread of linen, a little thick, and made of many turns, with a space of at least an inch between each turn; and have the patient hold the needle's head with both hands, and draw it towards a scent so that it comes into the back of the throat; and children in schools often do this, and it is a light thing to someone who wants to do it; then take the head that comes through the nose in one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth in the other hand, and pull them apart while holding onto the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as much as you know the wound has corrupted the flesh, then remove the filth, let out the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian oil, and put it back in its place just like before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrupt all that remains of flesh; and then put on a clean bandage some days until you are healed, and if you need dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purify the head, to which one distills oils and medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it can be made of silver or lead, resembling an open lantern like a candle, and it is used in the same way. And if you see fit, make a closed lantern, and have the instrument full to purge the head; and let there be a handle at the top to hold when heating oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the skin above the navel
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Sometimes a disease called "telul" arises on the navel and grows and becomes large at times, to the point where it is visible with the naked eye; and therefore you should have it removed from the beginning, and cut out all of the flesh around it, then apply the hot cautery or medicine on top of it; and if one delays cutting it until it has grown large, beware that it may be hard, of foul color, of poor sensation: do not touch it with iron at all because it is an enchanted abscess, for when you cut into it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of clean appearance, not of foul color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, then the patient will feel empty and the wound will heal well with things drying up and constricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the navel is cut open and cleaned
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when a solution of continuity comes in one of the cartilaginous works, it gives little profit, worse than in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to do what happens to anyone, if you look and see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring together the two lips with a suture, and heal it until it is healed; and if the lips are already dried up from one part and another, you must scrape off all the parts of their crust as long as they bleed, then assemble the two lips with a suture, and bind them, and sprinkle on powder of dragon's blood and burnt incense; and put on top of the powders a piece of a solid poultice or other soldering poultice, and leave it until it crackles by itself, then heal it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of stitching is that you assemble the skin with:
des apostemes des levres	Abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home they often get abscesses in the lips that are hard and resemble grains of mustard, smaller and larger ones; then you should turn your lips inside out, and cut each one with a needle and cauterize it with vinegar so that the wound is closed; and then let the lip heal on its own, and treat the area with dry things until it's healed.
de la char des gencives	from the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often there is gum tissue that grows on the gums, which the ancients called "albulus"; if it needs to be removed, you should hold it with tweezers and cut it at its root, and let blood or pus come out; then apply vinegar to the area, or other constricting and drying powders; and if that gum tissue comes back after being incised, and often does, you should cut it a second time and cauterize it: if it doesn't come back after being cauterized, those are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are assembled at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, scabs that are ugly and harsh; and sometimes the tooth is black and yellowish and green, until corruption comes to the gum, and it is stinking. You should make the patient sit in your hands, and their eyes be on you, and pull out the teeth or scabs as soon as they appear, until there is nothing left; and do the same with the blackness and yellowness and greenish color and other spots, until they are clean. And if you take out what is at the first reason, it's good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have cleaned everything. And know that teeth need various forms of instruments to be cleaned, according to how the work shows it, because the scrapers used to scrape away from the teeth have other shapes than those used to scrape between them; and these forms and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of its pain that you wait as long as possible to extract it, because it should not be done hastily; for it is a very high risk that there is no excuse for extracting. (This text suggests that the medieval dentist was being cautious and advising patients to delay extraction, possibly in an effort to avoid taking out teeth unnecessarily.)
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When then the patient is constrained to be drawn, it behooves you to be certain about the depth of extraction.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the pain will leave the patient, and they think it is because of a good tooth being drawn, and have the healthy tooth extracted; but nevertheless, the pain does not depart from them until the bad root is removed, for we have already seen this happen to those who are saints; and when you are well certain about the depth of extraction, it behooves you to scrape around the tooth on all sides in a strong spatula so as to protect the gum from all parts; then move it with your hands or fine pincers at first point and point, until they are well loosened, then firmly hold the pincers; and the patient's jaw should be between your knees, and keep them still so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push it inside from each part lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and eaten into, you must fill it with cloths, at the place where the hole is; and if you constrain it subtly with pincers, so that it does not break when being constrained; and you must work skillfully around the gum to uncover the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and inform the patient that through the evil of the root there will be greater pains than at first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware that you do not act thus as foolish doctors who by their haste and boldness break the root sometimes, and do not bring about what we have said; but sometimes bring on a great sickness through the roots that remain, or through the root that they break, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is torn, wash the place with vinegar or with oil and salt; and if blood comes out there, which often happens, fill the place with vitriol paste; and if this does not help, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	It seems like the text is describing a specific type of dental instrument used to extract teeth. The translation continues:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick limbs so that they do not bend at all, and let them be iron plates well made, and let them be held by teeth to keep them in place.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root stays on the opposite side, it is necessary that you put a dampened cotton cloth or butter there for one day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the joint is inflamed, then you put the forceps called "algefri", because the head seems to be a sharp jaw; and they are made inside in the same way as an awl and that is their shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out with those pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the flesh all around the root, and put in the instrument called "althali", i.e., pincers, by which this is its shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root jumps out through this, it is good; if not, you should use all the instruments, by which these shapes come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if that doesn't help with this instrument that has two rings, by which this is its shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other bandages that are placed in front of the teeth, and this instrument which resembles large pincers, the shape of which is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is useful only in that it cannot break, and know that there are many instruments for the teeth; and also other instruments which are not counted; and wise, skilled masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their work and the disease show them, for there are such diseases where the ancients did not teach a single instrument because of the diversity of them; and one should not break the chariot or the other bones unless it is necessary, or if he seeks the instruments that are needed, as I have told you, and with gestures, the form of which is as follows:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they are large and well-holding to hold the bone so it does not escape, but can hold and remove it; and then restore the place of the medicines fitting for this, and if there is putridness in the bone and it is small, then let all of this instrument be used:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural shape and the form is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know whether the tooth is newly grown after the tooth, and is not in its right place, and cannot be filed or smoothed: then make a groove. And if it is uneven with the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is as follows, and resembles one small beak, and is made of iron with an acute point at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in one's hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to be filed, take a file like this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is also like sharpening needles; and when you sharpen the point of a tooth, do it little by little in light hands so that it does not move until it takes shape; then finish with a smooth plane, and if the teeth are too sharp and hurt the tongue, you must whet the roughness until they are even, so that they do not hurt the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front tooth is loose due to falling or percussion, and the patient cannot close it over what they eat without it falling out, and you have treated them with restrictive medicines and this does not help; then it needs to be restrained with a thread of gold, because the threads of silver become green and rotten, but gold never changes; and the thread must be middle-sized, not too thick or too thin, according to the space between the teeth; and if you wish to move the teeth, take the thread and put it double between the two healthy teeth, then place the tooth between the new ones, as many as there are up to a healthy one on the other side; then reapply the covering until the part where you began, and strain your hand gently and carefully, as long as it does not move; and tie your thread at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the keys of the file to a pair of pincers, and assemble them, and reattach between the healthy tooth, and put it in such a way that it does not harm the tongue; and then let it be so tight as long as it can stay, and if it comes loose, or the threads break, tie it with another thread; if it stays and will serve thus for all his time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, such as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, you should replace it in its place, fresh from the bone, just as we have said; and let no one who is not skilled and careful intervene; and sometimes the shape of a jawbone's tooth is formed, and it is placed in the location where the defect is, and it is tightened just as we have said, and it stays in place and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to uncover the ligature of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	At times this string comes from under the tongue or nature, when it appears thus; or by accident of a healed wound; and the works are such that you work on the mouth of the patient, and have his head in your healthy one, and lift up the tongue; then take the nervous string of large forceps, as long as the tongue is freed from its seat, and if there is hardness or knot, and it is a sudden heal of a wound, put in the liniment and take with the large forceps that ligament; and be sure that the crack is not too deep, for the artery that is underneath; and when you have done this, lift up the point of rose water and of ice, or of cold water, then place under the tongue a tent of linen; and let the patient tie it every night, so that the wound cannot heal.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding comes from the incision, then place on the wound vitriol plaster; and if the blood does not cease, then cauterize with a slow cautery, which is good for this; then cure with another treatment until it be healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the growth is white or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards the groin, and there is moisture, then throw away the unguent, and make a fine paste with vinegar, and deliver him from both sides; and if the bleeding stops at thy work, then put vitriol plaster on top until it be stanchied, then return to thy work until thou hast removed all impurity; then lift up the powder of eggshell and rosewater, and cure him with other remedies until he be whole.
des apostemes de la gorge	Il semble que le texte soit une traduction ou un résumé d'une partie du "Régime du corps" attribué à Guy de Chauliac, médecin de Charles V du roi d'Arles (1347-1380).
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there come within the throat swellings called "godath", and one properly calls them almonds, and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then beware: if it is a hard abscess of little sense and fusse color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also on account of the bleeding; but leave it alone until it be dead, and then you will cut it out, lest it break off by itself; and if it is of white color again, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to cut, but first look if the abscess has cooled down and is appeased.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit in front of the sun, and his chest be bare, and the practitioner should open the mouth and take hold of the tongue between his hands, and press the tongue down with all the instrument, as to which is its form; and it should be made of subtle silver or fine bronze like a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue against the whole instrument, and you see the abscess, then take a wick and stick it in the almond, and the thread will be above as much as you can; and leave nothing of the threads with it, then cut at the instrument, which is its shape, that looks like a fist; and although the tip is curved, and one end the other, and are very sharp, and is made of iron or lead:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	Je pense que j'ai compris la traduction ! Voici :
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it should be cut on one side and named on the other; and when you have cut one of the almonds, then cut the other in the same manner, and after incision gargle the patient with hot water and warm oil, and scented waters which cause blood to flow out, so gargle the patient with water or with cooked pomace of pomegranates, or myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the blood is stopped; then cure as long as it is needed; and sometimes other swellings appear in the throat than the two almonds, so cut them in the same way as the two almonds are joined.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born within the throat, namely the small abscess; and I had well closed up all the throat so that the woman could not exhale through the obstructed passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and she would have been dead if she had remained thus for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had risen so high that it had forced out two pus-filled boils through the two openings of the birth canal.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I acted quickly then, and put an onyx in one of the openings, then the boil burst, and a large portion of pus came out; then I refilled the other part through the other opening of the birth canal, and I opened up the mouth and pressed the tongue; after that, I put the onyx into the abscess, and it started to bleed a little bit; and thus was unclogged the passage of the throat of the woman, and she began now to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscess grew again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, so much that it became very large; then I drained it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stayed without growing; and I left those parts, and knew only what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	It seems like you're trying to translate something from an old language or text.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When swelling occurs under the eye, and it is bulging and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is under a thick and rounded one, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the post-emerald is calmed down, and it is subtle, then it is necessary that you cover it; and the one which is thick assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of red color or black, then it is necessary that you avoid the incision to it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger over the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its swelling and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument which we have made remembrance of beforehand; then insert the needle into the eye and pull out the swelling, and cover it with the two instruments which I have said in the incision of the almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cut too much beyond the natural limit; for if you do, it causes great harm to the voice and tongue; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear about cutting, then you should use artifice in the cauterization of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your blood, and then presses the tongue against the instrument which we have said in the chapter of cautery, and mixes with hot sharp vinegar, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and put on the handle of this instrument, by means of which is its form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	Take the instrument that is used for putting on medication, such as a spoon or a syringe, and put the instrument to all of the medicine on the eye; and the patient should lie down on their side so that the saliva and mucus from their mouth go into the medicine inside, so it does not descend to the throat and the wound; then hold your hand over all of the medicine and press it onto the eye for the amount of time of half an hour, until you see it darken and the irritations from the medicine are calmed down. And if you see anything, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and put the instrument into all of the cotton on the back of it, so that the cotton hardens onto the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then let it dry, and wait for later.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is cured by fumigation in this manner: take camomile and yarrow and origanum and rue and chamomile and wormwood and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and put ash in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well glazed with strong earth, and inside the pot have a tool fashioned like a comb according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it be of silver or lead, and let one of the needles be placed in the patient's mouth so that the vapor rises to the eye through the thread, until the eye is numbed; afterwards it often recurs, until the eye dries out, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the coming of the hot abscess, for many things happen; and do not do this unless at the declination of hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a thread and put inside the patient's head a quill of egg white, so that the patient's mouth does not get too hot; for the quill of egg white does not allow the vapor to harm the mouth, and it is good cure together with salvation.

Or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of bread dough, or a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge with a thread, and then have them swallow it; and when it comes up, it will be hard, and then you can take it out; and if it does not come out through that which we have said, then take a instrument made of cloth according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the head so that it can enter the throat more easily and have the head raised upwards. And take care not to touch the epiglottis, lest everything comes together against you or you push the bone inside; and it is worth noting that the patient themselves should insert the instrument, because they are best able to feel if the thing has come out or not. If they insert it downwards, or pull it out at all the instrument in equal parts, until it is completely out.

Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters about abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscesses are there, according to what the remembrance comes afterwards from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and it is in two manners of which one is in its own likeness itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for those places where they are within the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the abscesses of the fat part are different from those which come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses which should not be pierced until the boil is dead according to its completion; and those of this kind that need to be pierced when they are thick, and do not die according to their completion, such as abscesses near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints and are left until they become green around them, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint may be corrupted, which is a cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is near the principal member and you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal member; or it is near the fundament, so that when you pierce it as soon as it is dead; and it does not seem right to you to pierce a hard abscess without digestion being completed, lest that one which is near the fundament should become green inside and form an ulcer; and could not heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the sign of perforation of the abscess that is dead according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the diminishment of pain and redness, and of fluctuation and of hardening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and you must do the perforation in a place more dependent on the location of the abscess, and where it seems to be softest; and make the perforation long enough to reach into the body, and if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or near joints and nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no skin covering.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these places, depending on the other member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the fatty part of the body, it is advisable that you leave the puncture open until it has been completely digested, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you close the punctures before it is completely digested, the body will fill with poison from it, and it will be full of bad humors; and perhaps the edges will become hardened and the bottom will become deeper.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that needs to be punctured according to the size of the body part, according to what the member in question requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you should make small punctures in small abscesses, and large punctures in large abscesses, and many incisions according to the likeness of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where it is necessary to split the core, and cover them; when they have become as hard as a cloth, and are swollen, then you should do just as one does with boils: and if there are such that are cut into three angles, and if there are such like the leaves of myrtle, as abscesses of the armpits; and if there are such where one makes a circular incision, and other cuts and forms of incision.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it must be that you thoroughly pierce; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and it has thickened a lot of flesh, and you pierce it, then do not draw out all the flesh in that hour, but rather take out part of it; then stop the abscess up to the next day, then take out something from it again; do this by little bits over time, as long as the flesh comes out entirely; similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or women, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus is shaken out at times with the issue of the flesh, so that by chance the patient dies, and you do not notice.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, let the wound drain, and see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a clean incision, then bind it with linen threads or old cotton; and if it's large abscesses, and there are many pores, it is necessary that you sew in each one a cloth so that they come together against each other; and if you have cut off from the abscess a part of the skin, and you have wrapped it around, it is necessary that you fill it with old cotton or a wad of linen free of moisture, and tie it up until the next day; then remove it, and heal it with ointment as long as it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is a bleeding in your work, then moisten with cold water and vinegar easily, and soak the cloth in it, and place it on the place bleeding many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, then apply a remedy and care, and the powders that I have said to be good for wounds in this book, and since it is the summer time, and the place or abscess is very moist and nervous, then it is necessary that you put on warm tents and wet cloths in wine and hot oil; and since it is winter, and the place is fleshy, then it is necessary that you put on wet cloths in water and oil, or in cold wine, until the third day, as we have said; and then loosen the abscess and its pus and treat it, as is necessary, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre. des soros	of wounds
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Where small abscesses come under the head, and they are of the kind that are like nets, just as the wool of a goat is, and there are many similar things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some which are fatty and similar to those where there is moisture like boils; and if they have such that are hard and stony when cut into, and there is no doubt whether the surgeon will make it worse.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of cutting is that you try out every instrument which is called "entromissoire", from which its shape comes after, what thing it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then make a cut on top of the long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape off without leaving any skin that contains that moisture, for it comes back again if you leave anything; then dip in Egyptian ointment, if it's present; if not, in water and oil, and apply the dressing to the wound, and let it stay until the next day; and those who are left of the night will run off.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then again renew the lint, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you know well that it does not remain in the night; then treat the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a lot of pus, then cut it out according to this form, from long; and throw away your splinters, and scrape off all around, and put all your cure to drain through the shirt where it lies; and if the artery gives you trouble, do what I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do likewise with the abscess if it is filled with stone, and from cutting and curing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the cut above the stony abscess and the moist one, if it is lighter, because they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or heads have no moisture, and one of the abscesses that I cut out from a woman's head was like a hard, sharp, white stone, and could not break; and if anyone had touched it, they would have just as well made an open wound like one.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	Other abscesses coming from the head, such as those which come to the heads of children and to the roots of ears, should have their opening always lowest in place, so that moisture may exit; and they are cured in the manner required.
des scrophules	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet !
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur in the neck, and under the armpits, and inside the groin, and sometimes they come in other parts of the body, and are swollen, and are joined together one with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly under its cloak, such as the boil and the abscess of the head, such as we have said; and the similarities to these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are tumours that contain moisture, and some that are malignant which do not wish to obey good health.

In that one then which you see of good condition to touch with the hand, and it is similar in color to the flesh, and is quiet from all parts and is not irritated by the nerves of the neck or artery or conduit, and it is not deep; it is necessary for you to cut it open on top, and scrape off every part, and take hold of the two lips of the core with a needle, if you need them, as we have said about abscesses of the head; and pare it bit by bit, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, nor make an incision that the hand escapes from, and do not look too far ahead, lest you cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and they do not let you work, then put vinegar or some powder that restrains blood in the wound, and hold the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed down, and the wound becomes softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is restrained, then come back to your work until you have completed it; and ask yourself if there are any small abscesses left, if you cut them and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure. Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.
