Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two bitter things: that is to say, the burning of the stuck flesh, and the drying out of blood and the evaporation of moisture; then treat moistened tents in mud or in a cow's gall, as long as the place spits pus, and let the burned flesh flow into the pus; then treat the wound with ointments that harden rough flesh, and are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healed, then it does not come back again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes just to the bottom of the fundament and is distant from the body, then block it with a cork or plug at the fundament, and question those.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tumor, and between two is the web or the sac or vessel, where it is near to bursting, so there is no fire that sees faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three manners: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it up to its base, or if you can see I put tents and cure as first; and do not go too deep in farth, that you do not cut the tent that holds the fundament, and come the egestions by the sense unwilling; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and cleanse since it is cut near the fundament, by probe or by another instrument appointed; then clean out that vessel which is in the wound, so long as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part beyond the fundament: if it were more easy thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And at any time fistulas are made in this manner: and it is when you puncture the tent in the fistula, and it is on one side near the base close to the skin above, so take a perforated tent as the head according to this shape.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put 1. thread twisted in 2, and I insert the tent into all the thread in the fistula as far as it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perforated in the margin of the base inside, then draw out the thread from that puncture, just as you pierce your needle or base; and pull out the head of the thread, and bring together the two ends together, and hold one to the other, and let it be for a day or two; and then bind it once more, until the threads close in between them, and are joined; then treat the wound so that it is sutured and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then make it pierce in all ways that you can, as long as it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it is not necessary to make it pierce so deep that the thread cuts through, and then treat it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spine-bone from which one makes the fistula is very narrow on one side and incised; and on the other side not, for that which one should not pierce at all, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the sinewy ones.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Worms are according to II ways: or they are inside the fundament, like a grain of resin, and there are small ones and great ones, and in the core they flow blood, and there is one or more, and they are outside the fundament and at the head of the fundament; but those that are outside so have much moisture, and in the core either a drop of clear water or a drop of blood, and they have the color of flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the fundament, is that you command the patient to sleep so that the fundament may issue forth, and the son will be seen; if it hastens, and you take with tweezers, or you hold it with your fingernail, then cut off in their roots; and if the threads cannot hold for their moistures, take them on a napkin, or on cotton, or on a piece of chamelot; and extract to your arms, then cut, and powder over some warm powders that are available instead of cautery; or you cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure with other cures until they be sound; and if the fundament cannot issue, cauterize the patient with a biting and harsh suppository so that what is inside the fundament may come out clearly; for when the patient feels it, and the thread is forth from the fundament, it is easy to cure; and it is thus: you take them on your fingernail or with tweezers, and cut, then cure as we have said, until they be sound, and fear not incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you bring the thread according to this manner: take a twisted thread and stick it in a needle, and then pull the thread above and make the needle pierced from the other side, and turn the two sides of the thread below the needle, so it be of good width; and tighten the thread firmly, then knot the thread, and extract the needle, and do likewise with all the others, and leave one end to permit the superfluity of blood; then put on the foundation a damp cloth in rose oil or cerote, and put on the foundation, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let them lie until they cease bleeding, and when they are fallen, cure them with ointment and other treatment, until they be healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the dryness of the fistula or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there has been dryness of the fistula in the intestine, and by natural constriction, and when the disease is old and medicine is useless.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you reset the point of a splinter or at your nail the scab above it which does not let it become moist; then cure it until it becomes sound as it behooves; and if it cannot dry out, then repeat the scraping stronger than before, until it heals well and is scraped off; then cure it until it be healed.
dou fremit	of the fistula (or a sudden onset of it)
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A small, false appearance is Formice, and it goes deep into the body; and sometimes it freezes, and one feels it just like a dead tremor, and comes throughout the whole body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a cord from an owl's feather, or a strong goose quill, and put that cord on the tremor, until it surrounds the entire tremor with purple circles; then turn your hand around the entire cord until you cover the entire tremor, and insert the tremor deep into it, and tear out the tremor by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is necessary, do the same with a cord of bronze or iron in this shape, and be subtle under and thread on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	don't pierce it, so that it can be held with the fingers, and press it. And if you see that it is necessary, cauterize the furuncle, as is written in the treatise on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of a purgative
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	At times they make a purgative of silver or mercury, or molten bronze or copper, and at times they make these small and large instruments in the same way as they are intended.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	So those that are made for the treatment of children and those who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of a purgative, whether small or large, is as follows: the belly is closed in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and it has an obstruction or the belly is constricted, as you see, and the head is pierced from within; and it has two perforations on one side and one on the other; and the belly should be stuffed with medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and it should be pierced all around with small perforations, and there should be a space of a thumb between each perforation, then insert into these perforations a strong thread of twisted hemp fiber in a cross shape, and gather up the belly like a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then purify with an enema; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the blister with oil or hazelnut of egg yolk or a similar thing, then insert it lightly; then the minister should squeeze the blister with both hands together until it is entirely empty, then extract the blister, and lift the patient's legs up high, and if the medicine wants to come out, so let it as long as it can; and if he sleeps one whole night, then it is a greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge the patient for the disease of purging the belly, and the medicines hurry to come out, then repeat it until they are healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are on the fundament or abscess, then let the blister be as subtle as for a child; and this is the shape of the subtle blister on which the skin is strained.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the section on the treatment of wounds; now we will say the treatments for hands and medicine, according to fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse in accordance with how they were made, and in accordance with the place or location where the wound was made, and what they were made by.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the piercing of a stone, and the cutting of a sword and a knife, or a lance or a club or an arrow, or similar things; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance comes in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, beware if it's from a blow of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is great, and you doubt slightly of hot abscess: if so do cleanse at once with cephalic remedy even if there is discharge of blood from the wound, and let the poultice be contrary to the injured part; and keep the patient repletion with wine and thick meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it will not cleanse, if the patient's meat is wasted, and does not drink wine, nor eat meat; and puts on the wound a hot compress, if an abscess comes, moistened cotton in rose oil or only wine, or if there is no hot abscess, if you put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder which I will say hereafter; and if the burn has moved it, if you put on some ointments, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the edges cannot be closed by stitching, then close them with sutures, just as I will say about the belly wounds, in the chapter on suture.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and it bleeds and only holds together by a thread, then close it; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace tough skin in place of soft skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meats, such as roasted testicles and bread, also chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find a corruption of skin that has not reached the bone, then close the corruption completely and let it bleed, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, cut it off, and it cannot be stopped by medicine, then tie the artery, and if you find it dislocated, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and that you put on this powder which heals even when the wound has become festering.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of this powder is such: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; and live calx three parts, and finely powder it, and apply the wound, and bind it firmly, until it is well dried and joins with all its blood; and then sew it up well, and let it be without untying, if it does not become swollen; for one should not remove the medicine as long as it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And at times one makes this mixture of calamine alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the wound has become festering and inflamed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the boil has moved the wound, even itself, do not put on this powder at all; but put on some digested ointments, or flour of barley made with water and honey, until it flows freely; then cure with other treatments until they are healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the break in the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then take out with delicate forceps; and I will tell you afterwards about breaks of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no distinction between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or the artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the hernia, then there is no other remedy except to leave the cure and not put anything restraining on it, for it harms hernias and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of hernias is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but if the medicine is strong, such as hollyhock leaf boiled in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and cucumber also boiled in sweet water, and other minerals used in this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and tie it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and high up and full of pus, then pierce them or lower down; and if the artery is cut, and there comes bleeding, then stop it, and bind it tight, and cauterize it as needed; and if the trachea bone is cut, or the airways, and you keep watch over it, so that the flesh goes on, then sew the wound over the base of the throat, and don't touch the throat but put it back in its natural shape; and then hold it together gently, and leave it for some days, then cure with ointments that are useless until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then clean it; and if there are pieces of bone, then extract all you can, and what you cannot take out, then leave so that the wound becomes foul and is opened up and attached to its issue; and if the wound is fresh, then powder over it with the powder I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has formed an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a wound from an arrow or knife, and the wound is deep, see if there are signs of festering in the wound that harm the patient: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, don't put powder on the wound at first hour nor tie it up to keep the blood from running out completely, and returning to the heart, and killing the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, put old cotton in the wound to suck away the moisture, and make the patient sleep over the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there's no spasming, nor evil tremors of the heart, nor strange happenings, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the patient with tentatives and other treatments, so long as they are well; and if they cannot heal, then know that there is a fistula; treat it thus as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut of sword or dagger, and it is simple, or worse on the back, then treat the surface; if it is great, sew it up; and if it is small, powder it, and if it is pressed into the bone and has broken pieces, clean out the wound and remove loose flesh; and if there are no loose fleshes, let the wound rot so that the extraction will be easier; and for other wounds on other limbs, make the same judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of intestinal rupture.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The ruptures of the belly are great and middle-sized and small; from a large wound intestines or their membranes often burst through which the introduction of them becomes difficult; and sewing is more difficult, and sometimes it is worse to treat a small wound than a great one, for that's why we put warm things into the intestines, so they don't enter too tightly, because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, and therefore it is better to sew the belly wound than others, two; know that there are four types of rupture of the belly: the two common stitches occur in the sewing up of the belly, and the stitching of other wounds of the body, and two other stitches proper are common to other wounds; however they are more proper with the sewing up of the belly, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and no thing from the intestines has issued out, and a grievous thing must be put back, this can be done in one of two manners: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is inflamed due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it in this manner: moisten a sponge or an old cloth with lukewarm water only, or cook in warm water with cypress and spikenard, and rub the intestine until the swelling is gone; and sometimes having done this, it stops restraining, and is moved that it was once for deflation.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with water or boil and mash the malvas, because by these means the entrance is cleared of something; and if it cannot enter, make a small pouch in the wound with the instrument used to lance empyema; and the first treatment is mindful that one should not cut without great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: cut inside along the curvature and outwardly not, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines have burst forth, then restore them to their natural form in their proper place, if you are able, for this is worth striving.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the part below the belly, then it behooves you to have the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, then put the head and chest higher than the parts below, and similarly arrange what I say for large and small wounds so that the part hurt be higher than the other; and thus it behooves to observe what I say about large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, put on the bandage that you have prepared, then take in your hands the medicated ointment which is applied to all the rupture in its hand, and bring together the lips; and this is the common manner of suturing, and it is for you to take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound's largeness, then leave the head of the wound a double thickness, and put in one needle where there is good strong thread; and pierce the two keys of the skin with the two keys of the flesh, which is inside the skin, until you make it penetrate from that part, and bring together the two heads of the flesh in four parts; then strain out a double thread around the needle of two parts, then bring together the two lips of the wound properly, and then leave a double thickness, and put in another needle; then tie the thread as you made the first needle, and do not cease to do this with needles until all the wound is closed; and let the needles be moderate, between fine and thick, for fine needles sew all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot well enter: therefore it is necessary that they be moderate; and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they cut and open the wound before the suture; then take out the heads of the needles, so they do not hurt the patient at night, and put tent or cloth on the heads of the needles to keep them, and leave them until the wound is sewn up; and this manner of sewing with needles is more advisable in small wounds, for it suffices one needle or two; the second suture is common, and it is for you to bring together the two keys of the skin and the two keys of the flesh together on one needle where there is a strong thread of moderate size; and when you have pierced these keys all four together, then take out the needle from the part where you began, in the manner in which men sew clothes; and leave a double thickness between each suture the thickness of a small thumb; this suture men know, and I sewed up a wound that was on a man's belly, which was hurt by a knife, and the wound was larger than a hand span, and the intestines were well two hands' breadth apart, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him back his intestines after he had been without them for 24 hours and the wound was sown up just to 15 days, and he cured it, and was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not cure him with ointment, for I was in a place where we could not find any, nor any medicine; and I applied clean linen to the wound two times a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and put its point from outside to inside; when it has pierced straight through in both directions, then leave the thread end or stitch where you had inserted the needle, and make it pierce from the inside towards the outside again, and the meaning of this stitch is that you sew just like a furrier makes pelts, and you leave the thread once on one side and take it up on the other until the stitching is completely finished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of stitching, which the Greeks call properly, is such that some people do who assemble the two parts together naturally, and apply one of the ends of the needle to the other end, in this way: stick a needle or end of thread close by, and make it pierce only that place, and leave the two ends of the thread; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part just as far as the inner part, through the two ends of the thread; then make it pierce one and the other from the outer part just as far as the inner part, in two other holes of the needle that are on the other side; and this is the more correct manner of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks say this word, and some testify it, that one should stitch the belly with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one should push one needle from one part, and the other from another, in the manner of those who sew corsets; and know that when the rupture is within the belly, then the stitching is more grievous than at other places in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, so long as the scab has not formed, then put on anew the intestines, and the cloth; then put on the powder made from charing wood, and if the scab has formed, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; then sew up the cut, and close the stitches, and the flaps; then cure the wound as you do with others, so long as it is healed; and if you have no medicines, then put on, at once when it starts to heal, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of another medicine in most simple dispositions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will not become community with the principal members, then it is necessary for you to soak linen lightly in tempered hot oil or in rose oil, and put it around the joints, and under the armpits; and if it feels pain or irritation in the intestines, and this often happens, then cleanse them with black wine tea clisters, and likewise if the irritation comes just up to the intestine; and make a hole within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is more easily healed than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are injured, and it is because of the fragility of their veins that are within them, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and the approach of its nature to those places.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the sinew springs out of the wound, put it back in place as with the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned yellow or black, you must tie the part that is black so that no bleeding comes from there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligament, and put the two bones hanging from the part below the wound as far as possible to ease the extraction when the sinew falls, and the wound will close.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the bowel.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, one can sometimes restore it in some men, because I have seen a man wounded by a lance; and the wound was to the right of the stomach, and it was infected and became an abscess, and there were diarrhea and windiness coming out of it; I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not stop until he was healed, and the area closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sew it, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his stomach; and there was no evil, but he remained in better dispositions, eating and drinking; and certain experimenters said that if he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be tied in this manner: take a strip of cloth from great thicknesses, then gather the lips of the wound together, and when the strip has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips so that it holds its mouth shut; and then strike the head with it, and it will stay so that it cannot be undone, then put another strip after in this manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	The head of the intestine is sewn together and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that has been cut from the intestine of an animal, in this manner: take the end of this thread from the intestine which is very well cleaned, and then tie it to the end of this thread with another thin linen thread twisted together, then push the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it tight in the seam; and this method of sewing with a strip is nothing other than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestinal grooves, there is no remedy or cure except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it becomes inflamed, is called "fistula" universally; and just as much so when it breaks out and runs with pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the virtue of a hard and white nodule that does not hurt, and is also broken out like the feathers of a bird; and sometimes it pours clear pus, and at other times thick pus; sometimes bloody, and at other times plentiful; and I have spoken already in the division of wounds, that every wound which is not healed and there is no flesh, is nothing but due to one of the nine causes: namely, due to weakness or scarcity of blood or body; or through malice; or because it has hard flesh inside, and on the skin, that does not allow new flesh to grow; or because there is too much pus; or the place is corrupted, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or due to the property in the region being slow in digestion and slow in healing, and tending towards pestilence by nature; or it has veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	And now it is fitting that I make you aware of the treatment of fistula which is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body. For there are fistulas which come to the great veins and arteries and nerves or to the syphac or intestines or bladder or to some of the ribs or to the spine of the back or to any joint of the hands or feet; and so too those which come to the principal part of the member and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas which are in this manner are of grievous cure, and there is no other way than to scrape and be ignorant; and if there is any fistula that does not come exactly to the place I have said, and you have faith in the cure and you can recognize it, then take a tent made of lead or iron; if the fistula is straight, search for it; and if the fistula is twisted, seek it out with a subtle probe of bronze, because the bronze bends around the twistiness; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well search for it with probes, then irrigate through one of the holes, because moisture flows from one hole to another, and cleans it; then incise bleeding according to your power, knowing whether there are bones or nerves, and it is deep in a place, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it; and when you know truly the place where it is, and if it is far from a jointure, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then cut according to what I have told you, and remove the faultiness and the corrupted flesh that are inside; and then cure until it is healed, and if the fistula is well dug into the right place, it is necessary that you dig further, as much as you can, then put moistened tents in medicinal aloe, and insert them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity which remains at the bottom; and then apply ointments of fresh, clean fat, until they are healed; and if they are not healed by these means, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, cut out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not cut or harm the main members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, so wash it until the corruption is completely removed, then cure with concoctions of fresh flesh until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and swells back up like before, know that you are not going far enough: dig deeper and search until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	Know that if not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot reach it; if there is no other remedy than to let nature take its course; and if there is only a little corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with forceps, then pull it out with an appropriate instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, do not leave any; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut and scrape and flesh, and deliver the bone.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, so place a poultice on the wound that will draw out putridity, and leave it until the flesh is putrid around the bones, and then they will have loosened the bones; and if it's a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, so clean only the corruption until the blackness is all gone, then repair the wound; and if there is great part of the corrupted flesh, and comes just to the marrow of the bone; so you must cut out and scrape everything right up to the corruption, and then cure it until it is sewn together; and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, which you can take as an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body, so much so that the matter came to his leg, and he became swollen with a large abscess, and had no external reason for it to open; but the surgeons, through their foolishness, worked on it so much that the abscess opened up, and they drained out a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and many holes came out that all poured out bad-smelling pus from the body; and many surgeons put treatment around two years, and there was no wise one in the art of surgery until I was called to him, and I saw his leg and the medicines with which they were treating him, and the matter that was draining through the holes in great quantity; and the body of the young man became red, and had a yellowish-green color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and I found that one was facing the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried then, and cut into one of the holes until I uncovered a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and pierced, and the corruption went right to the bone inside; I took out what appeared from the corrupted bone, and thought there was no other corruption, except for what I had removed; and I started to heal the wound with medicinal salves over a long time, but it could not knit together; and then I restarted, and uncovered the bone again as before, and I found the corruption continued in the bone, and I took it out, and then I thought to sew up the place; but I couldn't until I cut around a palm's length of the bone, and pulled it forward to its normal position, then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and sewn together quickly, and there was no need to start again over except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and because of the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For it was that often the bleeding led to evacuation of blood, but he became entirely cured, and in place of the bone there grew a hard flesh, and it turned out to be of good disposition and caused no harm nor any adverse effect at all, neither when he came nor went.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any place of the body, then it must be set thus: take a cord, and stretch it at the head of the bone which is open, and command someone to hold it up; and put another linen cord thicker than the first cord, and tie it above the flesh that is over the bone, so that you pull out the corrupt flesh below, and uncover the flesh on the place where you see it must be set, so that the setting does not hurt the flesh; and take a hot trowel or a flat stone below the bone to kill the corrupt flesh; and it must be set as much as can be seen and felt the corruption, and it must be set again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh entirely; then put a hot iron underneath, and then thread from one part to the other the corruption, and the threading should be as long as the length of the corruption, just as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut out the corrupted joint, and thread the bone where it contains on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuity of two joints, then there is no other remedy but to cut; and if the corruption is in the wrist of the hand or in the wrist of the foot, then that thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must inquire into the corrosion how it presents itself; and purify it in all the ways that you can, but do not let the vein or the nerve hinder you; and know that the incisor and the threads for cutting these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their largeness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare an instrument for each similarity of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of the diseases; so think about the instrument which you need according to what it requires.
dou feu	from fire (i.e. a hot iron or ember)
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints can be harmed either internally or externally; and when you have medicated that harm with the treatment of medicines, and it does not benefit, then you must cover that member up to the place where the harm comes from, so that the patient escapes by this means from death, or by the malice, which is greater, of the defect of the member; and the signs are such that the member becomes black, so that it seems to be burnt by fire, and then after the blackness, the corrosion goes on from member to member, and takes hold throughout the body; if you hasten to cover it up, and this is due to the bite of certain venomous beasts, such as sea scorpion and viper and similar things, if the corruption is in the head of the eye, then cover it, and do not give any hope of coming down to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes down to the hand, then cover it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover it up to the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, it is death, and there is no remedy except for the measure of its virtue; and in just this way do when the corruption comes on to the foot: if it comes to the first joint, then cover it after the other joint; and if it reaches the foot, then cover the whole foot; and if it rises up into the leg, then cover at the knee joint; and if it comes from above the knee, then there is no other remedy than that the patient dies; and the manner of covering or soothing the member is such that you bind it on top and below, and stretch out one servant of the binding downwards, and another servant of the binding upwards, and you loosen the flesh which is between the two bindings to a span long, so that the bone be uncovered; then cover or soothe it, and put linen cloths on either side, so that the soothing does not touch the healthy place, and come again to the patient with other lesion and boilish swelling.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding comes from the incision, then cauterize the place immediately, or put some restraining powders on it; then come back to your treatment until it is complete, then tie the injured member with a suitable bandage, and heal it as long as it remains sound; and I will tell you what happened to my home in his foot: he got a burn that seemed like fiery ash, and that corrosion came first to his two feet, so much so that it consumed all the foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and was healed; and long afterwards the corruption came back to his hand, and he came to me, and I put on him things rebounding after the cleansing of the flesh, and the corrosion could not cease; and he asked that I cut off his hand, and I did not want to, because I had hope of rebounding the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the virtues of the man were weak; and he became utterly despondent, and went back to his land, and hastened to cover his hand, and was healed; and I have not told you this tale except because it is done another way, when one needs it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Occasionally an abscess forms in the fatty area, and remains for so long that it makes a large collection of pus; and then it rots and perforates, and the pus flows out, leaving the place empty, just like a wineskin; and the skin which is on top is just as fine as delicate drapery, and does not reach just to the bone, nor just to the nerve, and such diseases are called "sain", and are not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches just to the bone deeply, then it is called "fistula"; and the cure is that you cut around that skin all over, and similarly when it is fine, like delicate drapery; and one does not treat it for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you suspect that the skin is putrefying, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with fat, then cure it by enema thus: look to see if the breasts are large, and the bowels which come out are of foul odor, then make a Egyptian medicine enema in this way: take asafoetida, oil, and litharge, equally, and place the mixture in a vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes just as thick as honey; and then take some of it according to your need, and mix it with water and honey, and use it to enema the breast, and close the fistula; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then strain it out; do this many times, until the breast is cleansed, and the foulness is removed; and sometimes an enema of ash-water is made when this medicine is not present, and one takes ashes from a grapevine, and pours water on top, then lets it cool, and uses it to cleanse, as long as you know that the breast is well cleansed; and if the patient cannot endure it, nor the Egyptian medicine nor the ash-water, then make an enema of water and honey or oil with a small amount of litharge mixed in; or make an enema of honey and sweet wine, where the honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine causes the pus to flow out; and when you have done this, and you suspect that the breast is well cleansed, then make an enema with it that makes fat form in it, and do what I said about the properties of medicines or treating ointments; and if the fistula of the breast is small, and the canule of the enema cannot enter it, then enlarge it with a small iron rod, and place on top a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, as long as it is enlarged; and if the wound is too wide, then close it and leave only the space where the enema can enter, and if the fistula that emits pus is above, then cut or lower it to its proper place.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.
