Car when the bowstring is deep, do not let it grow loose; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you see, prepare in such a way that the bowstring goes to its lowest point because when the bowstring is deep, do not let it grow loose and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you see, prepare in this manner: so that the bowstring goes slightly downwards and does not leave anything of the bowstring; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and stand over the linen cloth that covers all the wound; then cut at the strongest point the skin of the breast to a depth more than the first time, then anoint with soothing ointment over the other cloth according to the size of the incision, and put it on the incision of the wound to loosen the bowstring, and do not take off the large cloth outside which afterwards will stay once; and that which is over the incision of the breast, take often to remove the bowstring, and know what comes out of the bowstring, whether it is venom or pus or much or little, or digested or indigested; and be careful if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this manner and you see the nature that seeps onto the incision of the wound, know that the bowstring has healed already, and approach the physicians; then loosen it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you loosen the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast spatters indigestible pus after many days, know that the breast has not healed.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons stay behind after a long time, do not despair of health, for the healthy approach.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are men whose wounds take a long time to heal, and those who do the opposite; and if undigested chyme bursts forth from the chest after many days, know that the breast is not cured; and if the breast takes a long time to dry up and is swollen, mix medicines dry in substance and dry in virtue, such as ointment of lily water, for it contains a great part of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take ointment of lily water, and make it with rose oil, and the ashes of old wine equal in substance; then boil it down and use it; and do the same thing as thickened boiled honey when the ointment of lily water is not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them, and powder them over the honey when it is on the fire; then put it in a cloth and apply it to the breast, and sometimes administer long Aristologus and celestial lily roots, which are also like flaxseed meal and centaury; and use simple or composite ones: grind them, and make powder, and put it over the honey I have said, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and is not cured by this cure, then know that corruption has penetrated deep, and made an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in ligaments; and thus perform the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the boil on the arm (ungle).
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A carbuncle is an abscess that forms beneath the armpit of the hand, or of the foot, or it may perhaps occur in other places; and when it has grown old, and one pays no heed to it, then the abscess becomes septic, and they run and flow with pus as long as they flow from the root of the boil, and perhaps they will flow entirely; and come gangrene right up to the bone, so that a foul pain comes, and the joints of the finger are wide, and the color is bluish.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit at all, then you must cut out from it entirely the surplus matter that is left of the boil, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great aid if the bone is sound and the boil is healthy; and if the boil immediately touches the flesh, begins to prick, and break out, then you must put the hot iron on the boil that pricks the flesh, push it up high, and cut out that subtle and delicate flesh, and put on the remaining flesh medicines that burn and corrode in order to remove all of it; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corruption is in the bone, so cut it out, and draw a thread through, for as long as the corrupt bone remains inside, it cannot heal; and if you see the nail corrupting, so cut it out with the instrument shown above, then cure it until it heals; and if it is full of pus and festering, and it feels great pain, so must you first clean it; then cut through the skin over the abscess, being careful that the knife does not come close to the flesh beneath the abscess, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on top which will soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of deafness in the hand.
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The nails which grow on the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy, and sometimes there is a toe in place of one, and occasionally an awn, and once in a while the birth is in the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of the nails.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born in any part of the navel does not move, and he who is born with the jointure of the navel, by chance may move; the birthmark of one who is fleshy is light, similarly: cut it in its root from a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those that grow at the root of the joint are difficult to cure, if you take it upon yourself to cut. (i.e. the procedure to remove the affected tissue is complex and requires careful consideration)
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In that which is born or stuck in the lower navel, it is necessary that you cut first around the flesh up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable string for this, then heal him until he is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The wounds that come to the bones in the joints occur by birth, or from a wound, or from being burned with fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the seam, so that it may be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or wet cloths soaked in rose oil, so they do not join together; or put between two thin pieces of linen until the place is healed, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If a wound comes to any of his knees with the palm, then bind that wound in the same way.
des vils	the ulcers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Swollen veins are large and inflated, full of superfluous melancholic humors, which occur in many members of the body; and more often appear in legs of those who walk and work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to them an occasional purging with vinegar, and then salve with the oil of basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with iron is in two manners: one is that you cut them and let out the black blood; and the other manner is that you tie a vein and let it bleed all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The incision is in this manner: first raise the leg with a hot iron very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned out, then restrain the patient's leg from above the knee to the part below the ankle; then cut the vein at I place, or II place, or III place, with an incision wide, then lift and let bleed out the black blood in your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can endure; and then tie it, and command him that he eats food going towards cold black bile; and repeat the evacuation and cleaning when the veins are full, and harm the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The swelling of the vein is done in this manner: cleanse the leg of the patient, if it has much hair, then put it in a bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it turns red and swells; and if you do not have a bath, heat it at the fire, and then tie a strip of linen around the vein near the knee, or in the area below the ankle; then open the skin on one end, and scrape off the swelling from both sides, so that it appears when touched; and it is seen red and black, and when it enters the skin, it seems like a white cord; then put the thread underneath, until it has come out of the skin, and then stretch it lightly with the needle, then tie another knot in its place; then scrape off the skin on top of the vein so that it appears, and raise it up to the first knot, just as you did before, and then attach a new strip, just as you did before, then tie another strip or more if needed, then raise it, and tie it at the foot, then pull out and raise until the second strip; then draw it out from strip by strip, so that it comes out completely whole, then tie; and if you cannot draw it out and lift it, put a needle in with a very strong double thread, and attach and draw it, and put underneath the thread, and turn your hand from one side to the other, until some of it comes out; and be careful that it does not split, because if it splits, it will not be able to be drawn or lifted, and harm comes to the patient; and when you have completely drawn it out, then put wool in vinegar and rose oil on the place of the wound; and cure until he is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and looped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you should cut it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron that is used to cut the vein should be curved, and not sharp, lest it cut the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were fine, it would cut the vein, but rather it should be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of civil veins
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or tree grow, and in dry land; and it may occur elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the corruption that comes under the skin, as it comes inside the body snakes and worms, inserted between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this swelling are such that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes, and the swelling begins to come out, just like a root from a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the swelling bursts, you must wrap around a piece of linen cloth that is one and a half to two ells in width, and the node, and let the linen be on the leg, and every time it comes to a point at the surface, then wrap it around the linen, and the node; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap up the rest, and do not cut it in its root, until it has come out entirely; for if you cut it, it will go back into the flesh, and bring about an abscess and rot at the place, and a bad disease; therefore, it must be treated little by little until it is gone, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this swelling, when it is treated over five palms long, or ten, has come to me, of which one came out from ten palms long, and when you cut it, blood and pus will come out, and the cavity inside will be empty, and then apply medicines that prevent rot any day, then it will cure itself like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at any time the vein opens with many streams, and especially when it opens in a joint of the foot or the foot itself, where there is much hemorrhaging, and from which blood spurts out; heal him then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "maladie de buef", because it has often afflicted cows, and it is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes all over the body rising and descending, and it feels one well from member to member, until it reaches the skin where it is going and bursts forth; and it is bred from corruption of certain humors, such as worms and serpents and lice and tapeworms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it reaches the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this has often happened.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and pulled out, one cannot force it to go until it wants: so you must then tie the place above and below with a strong thread tightly; then cut on top and pull it out, and if the worm is deep in the flesh and you do not find it, then cauterize with fire on top, until it boils; and the greatest harm that it does, is that it runs to the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming or its head near the eye, then hold below it a thread tightly, then cut on top, and pull it out; and the patient must be used in cleansing of body with dissoluble medicines for the bad humors arising, and warn him from putrid meat.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	from the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes in some members, and can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I looked again, and I saw it growing up as quickly as a worm on the shoulder, just like freshly minted silver when it is cut from its mold; the pain departed from that place, and fixed itself in the shoulder, and then it quickly spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; and she told me that it was often turning around the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this disease in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	However, I had thought many times that the pain would move from one place to another, but I did not see it so in the woman; and I thought to myself that it was because the woman's body was dry, and her veins were uncovered, and for this reason appeared that constrained movement; and they do not appear thus in those who are well-nourished, and have moist bodies and replenished veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears as we have said, then bind tightly above and below with a bandage; and then scrape on top until the swelling is forced to its place again; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your eyes, then cure it with those who relieve swellings, such as foul-smelling pills and serpent pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Splinters are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the places in the body where they lodge.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The differences of their kinds are that there are those with great points, and small ones, and barbed, and soothed; and those with two angles, and those with shafts, and those with pieces; and the one that lodges in any member does so in two manners: or it pierces a principal member, such as brain, heart, liver, lung, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls then in any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you later appears to you: then you should be careful with the extraction of this arrow, because the patient dies after in many dispositions; and when this bad sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not yet deeply seated, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and bursts the convolutions that are above the brain, is when there is scotoma and dullness and dizziness and turning and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and confusion of understanding, and vomiting of gall; and possibly there is discharge from the nostrils or the ears; and perhaps the speech and voice are lost; and there bursts forth a moist white boil from the wound, like a pustule, and also as if it were a piece of charred flesh; and when these signs appear to you, then beware of treating it, and pull out the arrow if it is not too deep.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of an arrow wound when it pierces the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in a hard object, not empty; and perhaps the arrow moves like hair does, and there is dark blood, and chills and cold sweat, and syncope: be certain then without doubt that death is coming.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the splinter when it lodges in the liver is that bloody foam bursts out from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the sick person changes color, and gasps for breath and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the splinter lodges in the covering of the stomach, it is near the small ribs; and causes great pain and great distress, and gasping for breath; and makes all the muscles of the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the splinter lodges in the stomach, perhaps something that is undigested meat comes out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the splinter lodges in the belly and comes out through the intestine without any signs of digestion, then there is no hope for a cure or for extracting the splinter.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the splinter lodges in the bladder and causes the urine to come out and flow away, and the sick person feels a great pain, then know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and armpits and spine of the back and forearms and calves and legs and similar parts, are safe according to various conditions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the splinter is in a nerve or artery and it is venomous, as I will tell you happened to me, so that you can do the same.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	An arrow struck him in the eye socket at the root of the nose: I treated it and pulled it out on the other side under the fat of the ear, and he recovered without a problem.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I pulled out an arrow from a game that struck him in the fat of the eye under the eyebrow, and the arrow was bent, and I could only pull it out as far as the shaft, and the arrow was great from a Turkish bow, all light iron without ears; the player recovered, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And draw an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was the Arab arrow with ears: I removed the fletching, and made it fine until I drew it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I drew an arrow from his home that was stuck in the belly, and he thought he would die; and then when he had passed XXX days, it did not change its position; I cut into the arrow, and extracted it, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you wish to remove an arrow that has stuck in the back of a man, and the wound was closed above; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change its natural positions, nor found any harm in any of his natural workings.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And if you see another man to whom an arrow has stuck in his face, and the wound was closed above; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And draw an arrow out of the home of Prince the King, which had stuck in his neck, and was slightly declinings to the right part; and was the arrow quite retracted. I was called for the cure after it had been stuck for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched it with a fine probe and did not feel it at all; and he felt pricking and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the point of the arrow I put on top of it a drawing ointment attractive and digestive, so that the place would not inflame; and the wound of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put the ointment on it for many days, and the wound resolved again, and the patient stayed thus for a long time, until he felt the arrow one day inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I apply medicated ague to the wound by hand daily, until it was open; and I tried it, and felt the head of the arrowhead which had hardened at its place; then I pressed into the opening of the wound with that medicated ague, as long as the head of the arrow appeared clearly visible; and the process lasted well for about four months, and then set in so badly that I inserted forceps there, from one side and from the other, and it could not come out; then I did not cease to subtilize and ingineer with various instruments, as long as I grasped it on the first day with good forceps, according to its form which will appear at the end of this chapter, so that I led it out, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the surgeons judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you place your cure on what I do not say, for books cannot grasp everything; but wise masters come from great little things, and from those present and failing, they find new work, and new instruments, at the descent of strange things which occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not shoot out of members or are stuck in them except in two ways: either from the place where they enter, or from somewhere else; and those that shoot out through the side where they entered, it is an arrow entering into a fleshy part, and shoots out one time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not shoot out now, then leave it alone until the flesh is rotten around it and the issue has been cleaned; and also if it is stuck in the bone and cannot come out, leave it thus for some days, and move it each day; and then it will shoot out, and if it doesn't shoot out, then make a small hole all around with a very fine instrument, until the area around is enlarged, and then pull it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes just up to one of the ventricles of the brain, and among the accidents that I mentioned earlier the patient is instructed: do not draw it out but let it remain until after some days when the hairs are even, for if the arrow comes close to the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone alone and does not go up to the brain, and the patient remains some days without bad accident, then the instrument for drawing it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very stuck in there and cannot come out, then apply hot poultices around, as I have told you; then treat the place until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is reset in its place in the body so that it cannot be seen, then search for it all around the tent; and if you feel it, draw it out with a suitable instrument; and if you cannot because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone nor nerve nor vein, then cut around the wound until it is large; and draw out the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has ears by which it holds, remove the flesh that is stuck in there on both sides as far as you can, and then break or bend the arrow's ears so that you can draw it out; and be careful not to break the arrow, so that you will draw it out more easily.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot get it out at once, leave it until the area around the wound is purged, then pull it out, because the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the hemorrhaging of blood makes you contrary, so administer that which we have said of the cure in its chapter; and be wary of incising a nerve and a vein, and take thought how you can remove the arrow without peril, quickly or tardily, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form he was when the arrow struck him, for it is the greatest aid that there is, and if you cannot, so put him according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another part, if it has pierced some thing of him, or the skin is swollen in place where one sees or feels apparently; cut then above, as much as the tongs may take hold, and then pull it out: if it springs back now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand roundly, so that it goes into the bone, and enlarge the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, so leave it still and then begin the extraction again until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is there, so push it all the way in; and if the shaft is broken, and you must administer poultice, so administer the instrument curved, so that the point of the arrow enters into the curve of the instrument; and then push it out, and if the arrow is bent, so insert the instrument at a pointed end in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is embedded, it is necessary that you cut out all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as is fitting.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow lodges in the head or side or belly or bladder or ribcage and is nearby and you can cut upon it then cut; and beware of cutting into a vein and a nerve, and then pull it out, and then sew up the wound if need be; and treat it until it is healed.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tweezers with which one pulls out needles are like the beak of a bird, and see here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways of it: great, small, and little ones, according to the quantity of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feathers of a bird, to guide towards the tip of the arrow, such as this shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of pliers in order to bend and test if this is so:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the strings of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are 31 veins by which one is cleansed, of which there are 16 on the head, namely: two pipes that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and two arteries that are in the two temples apparent; and two pipes that are in the two corners of the two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nape; and the two gullet-like veins that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips, above the mouth, and they are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are below the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly draws blood are V in each arm: the one is cephalic, and is on the left side, and they call the common people "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "femoral", and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic itself is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the navel, and it is that one from which one draws blood, which opens manifestly above the armpit.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the one that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and foot are three veins: the one is under the fold of the skin on the left side, and the second popliteal which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein that is called "sural", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bloodletting of the veins that are behind the ears helps old catharrs and migraines; and the quality of the bloodletter is such as I tell you, which is to raise the head of the patient and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then bind the patient's neck with a cord so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places of the head: if they are at your fingertips, take hold of them; then take the lancet and insert it below the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand up to the entire vein and cut through the skin and the vein well enough twice over, and let out the blood as far as you see; then bind and tie it so that it is healed; and I have already said incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if worth anciently to emigraine, and sode, and obtalmie accustomed, and at the core of tears sharp as eyes; and the quality of the bleeder thus is: for the patient stretches his neck so far that the two veins appear openly; and he feels the hairs below your thumb, then signs from above; then lift the knife above the vein to your thumb's tip, and insert the lancet below, and raise the vein upwards, and cut, as you have done in the other two veins, and make flow of blood according to your need; then release the patient, and put your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put on cotton; and then bind it tightly, and let it stay until it is healed; and we have spoken of their closure and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood of the vein in the forehead is worth as much as the blood of the cerebral vessel for ancient facial diseases, and migraine, and headache; and the quality is that the patient twists his neck so tightly that the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on top of the vein, and press with your hand or something else, and let two bloods come out according to what you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein so that it is tied and at no time does this work leave a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not good that the scars be too sharp; and the veins are crooked, because the bone is close, and perhaps the scar will break through when it becomes thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in the eyelids helps eyes and scabies, and headache, and erysipelas in the eye, and facial diseases; and the quality of their blood is that the patient twists his neck by some ligament, just as before; then let it bleed, and the bleeding will be like a thread, somewhat long and somewhat wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the scar is thin, it may break through; then let out blood as much as you need to, and then bind with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein near the neck is very useful for ague, and for a surfeit of water, and for face diseases, such as migraine and redness that comes in the face, and most especially when it is old; and the quality of the blood is that the patient will strain his throat, then hold his neck to your left hand, and take the subtle flame long, and put it among the palate which is between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will now begin to flow; and do not let it go too deep, and make the bleeding of the blood according to your necessity, then tie it up one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the two garters is useful for the constriction of the gallbladder, and for the beginning of ulcers, and for many diseases, and for empedine, and for corrodes, and for herpes, and for eczema; and the quality of the blood is that the patient will strain his throat under one and the other, as we have said; and let the master be standing over the head of the patient, and the patient sit on a seat, then bleed the vein of long a little bit wide, then draw out the blood moderately, or as much as is necessary; then make another cut in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and bind around the veins moderately, so that the patient does not strangle; and let him be until morning, when the wound will have healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the washing of books (or possibly "of book remedies")
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins on the upper lips helps to cool the mouth and corrupt the gums, and split the lips, and cause the nose to bleed inward.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of washing is to have the patient sit in front of you, and strain their neck as I said; then turn back their lip, and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, and recognize them by the fact that they are black, and by the small dark spots around them: cut both, and if you do not know them, and you have doubt, then cut the larger of each side; and do similarly for the two veins above and below, because it is the same manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the washing under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The washing of the veins that are under the tongue helps after the washing of the cephalic, and it is for the tightening of the throat, and for eye diseases, and mouth diseases; and the quality of the washer is that the patient sits between your hands in front of the sun, and lifts their tongue, and looks down each side for a black vein: wash one and the other, and do not go too deep, because under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the throat from which one commonly bleeds are treated in two ways: either they prick at all a large flaming myrrh, or a subtle olive oil like sharpened knives, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and subtle according to the largeness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the lancet is very well known, and it's large as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the thick-veined veins that are full of fresh and apparent blood, and that contain much blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the burning olive oil.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it's more delicate and pointed, and it's for bleeding the small veins where there is subtle yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The bleeding of the basilica, which is one of these veins, often helps with diseases that are below the throat, and under the neck, and under the chest, and under the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed skillfully, and to warn him away from the artery that is underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he severs the artery and blood flows out in a stream, then it is necessary to stop it, as I have said; and he should not prick with the burning oil, but cut so that it is "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica (vein) does not open clearly, it is necessary to draw out its contents, and change to another; or you wish for some blood from it, or make a cut into the vein in the arm: it opens clearly; and anesthetize with the flail, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you wish to know the location of the vein, it is necessary then that you draw out the arm, so that you touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the spot with ink, and bind the arm, and cut into the vein with the flail anesthetizer; and be careful not to hit the artery when you see the place inflamed, for it is the artery: remove it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it come out in the same way as the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is arterial blood: hasten then, and put your thumb on top for a long time, then remove your thumb if the bleeding stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and be cautious, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood doesn't stop and it's bothering you, and you don't have any medicine, then cut the artery if it shows itself, because the head of it is retracted; and cauterize the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a peel of fig tree bark and burn it, and take one half and tie it well just up to the other part; if the blood is stayed, that's fine; if not, treat with the powders that stay bleeding; and the staying does not harm in many dispositions for the small place of the wound, and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood of the vein in the middle so helps that it treats blood from the head above and the body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic, as we have said; and it behooves the squire to beware for the nerve which is below, and if he points too deep and he finds the nerve, and it swells and the bleeding will be hurt, and by chance may not heal; and this nerve opens up many times, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then it behooves you to take out the needle with haste; and protect the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the cephalic artery so helps, that it draws blood from the head, and aids the eyes; and one must bleed at the sharp olive oil place or the sharp myrtle flame, for it is the most safe of all the veins, because there are no nerves nor arteries under it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Anyway, one must seek the most gentle place, and harm nothing if one fails the first time, and then try again; and perhaps the place swells in some men, when one fails the first time, but it harms nothing.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding is according to your opinion.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding, is that bleeding is not done except to preserve health, and to avoid illnesses to come; and the bleeding should be done in one of the three veins that are in the neck: that is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and it should be bled in the beginning of spring, and in autumn, and after eating, when the sign of repletion appears; and it should be bled on the first or third day, after two or three hours from dawn.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who is treating the patient does not have a fixed time for administering treatment, but rather treats at any hour or moment as needed; and it is not necessary to treat children until they are 14 years old, nor women bearing fruit before the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the elderly be bled who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be treated, in whatever manner it may be, it is necessary that they have their intestines cleared with a gentle enema, if they have much feces retained, so that the veins do not pull out of the intestines harmful superfluities towards the main limbs; nor does the person heal who is too full of meat, or drunk, until he has been sober, nor those who are dropsical; and beware to treat someone after colic passion, and vomiting, and purging of belly, and multiple times with a woman, and labor, sleepiness, and work, and all things by virtue, either through arms or the body; then subtilize the humors, if the blood is thick, by means of food and drink and medicines, if you have the power to do so; then enter the bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and be healed from the pain around the third part, as we have said; and keep that day of work, and labor, and lust, and similar things away from him; and be joyful and happy, and let the physician stand higher than the one who is being treated, and wet the arms with a cloth twice or thrice, then bind the bandage above in moderation, for if it is too tight or loose, it cannot correct the blood; and then rub the patient's arm with his hands until the veins swell and can be felt; then wet the physician's hand with the flame of an old oilcloth; then place his right hand on top of the one being treated over the place where he wants to treat, so that the pulse does not falter or fail when striking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flow as quickly as strings to the surgeon, and there are some such that are filled with windiness; so that when one puts on the flame, it retreats from the flame, and cannot be opened up. And thus is one of them; and if the vein overflows, then the wound is too narrow, for this reason the surgeons should be aware of these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened on the first try, that's good; but if not, he should start again quickly, near or above that spot, if the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the lump is inflamed and the patient becomes frightened, let him be left for a day or two, and do not bind his arm: it may come to a warm abscess. Do not have him get in the bath, then resume the treatment if he wishes; and if the opening is small, cut it with a sharp knife and you will doubt that there is not as much blood as you see, so believe in this very same opening itself for all the flame directly; and do the work hastily, so that the lump may be inflamed; for such things have happened many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the place swollen, do not begin the surgery again, and apply a poultice of linseed oil to it, because it lightens the body from blood, and is a binder in this place that the oil; and thus administer the linseed oil in each incision that you make on veins, to stop the flow of blood; and do the same for treacle and bowel of eyes, when it is applied to the place; so subtly will the blood coagulate and separate as it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes to it, which has often happened, especially when the body is not yet fully cured of that time or the opening of the vein is small, then hurry and put a wet sponge on the place in water and wine with a little warmth, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the blood has come out of the vein, and if some blackness or greenness remains at the place after some days, it will not harm him; and if you wish, put something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in vinegar, mastich, or similar on it.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there has been an abscess and appearance after the bleeding from the basilica vein: therefore put your hand on it, and if you find the area soft to the pressure of the hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, beware that you do not apply anything from what we have said, for it may cut short the vein's blood supply; but make a dry poultice to harden the area, then cover it with another dressing until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each bleeding in proportion to its quantity and virtue, and according to the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see a lot of it, let it continue to flow until it becomes more subtle; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	It is necessary to that person who is pale and weak, and has need of bloodletting, to make a larger wound, and the incision be wide; and for that person who is feeble, do the opposite, and have him healed by small cuts, often and frequently, and it must be healed by cutting obliquely, not by pricking; and this manner of healing preserves from the decorruption of blood and the covering of nerve, and is more useful than a long incision or a wide one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for that person to whom the body fails in bloodletting, it is necessary to give wet bread soaked in apple juice; if he is overheated, then bleed him three or four times with the cup; and if he has a cold complexion, then mix wet bread in sweet syrup, or aromatic honey syrup with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he vomits at the sainie, after the spilling of much blood, it is necessary that he drink a broth of meat and a sweet-smelling syrup and use other things which we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to move his arm and heal another time, so it must be, when it is weakened by great blood loss, that he heals gradually little by little, according to the quantity of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to move his arm after the first healing, and he has strong vigor, then it heals within 7 hours after the first healing, or within the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal from another side, then he must heal on the second day or the third.
