Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot abscess and redness and pain and swelling have completely gone away, and you need to continue with poultice and bandage, then start again as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the member any of what we have said, then do not untie it until after three days or four or five or seven; and at no time leave it for twenty days, as is seen, so that the bruise becomes firm and approaches the skin above; then restrain it more than before, and its flesh swells, as I said before; and if you see the area dry faster than necessary, know that swelling cannot come to it; therefore heat a cloth in hot water each time you untie it, and do this every other day, and apply one poultice of the liquid; by this work the swelling is cut from the member, and quickly correct what the foolish doctor did, who left the member twisted: that's bad, and it's painful work, and I see nothing else but to loosen and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	It seems like the text is concluding with a heading "des diverses manieres de brisure", which translates to "of various manners of breakage" or "of different types of fractures". This suggests that the author is about to discuss or describe various types of breaks or injuries, possibly in preparation for discussing treatment methods.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many ways of fractures, and various figures, and the causes are assigned; for there are fractures that are made by striking with a sword, and the arm breaks all the bone down to the splinter which is under the bone, just as does a hatchet or an axe; and because of this it is called this manner of breakage "hacking".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone above without piercing it, and is called this manner of break "absolute"; and the wound of these two breaks is large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it's a crushing blow, or a splitting break, or from the back of the arm with stone, or falling on stone, or other similar causes.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it's a comminuted break, which approaches just to the periosteum that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that has healed in the bone just as subtly as a hedgehog, and the crack is small, and because of this it is called this fracture "capillary"; and if the wound which was made either by piercing with an arrow, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes enter the piece of the bone downwards, and there is a hole like those that coppers make when they hammer above their cauldrons; then it is said to have entered inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those who have loose bones in their skull, such as the head of an infant; and it occurs in all these manners of fracture where small pieces are broken off from them like that; and I will speak about it in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breaks by the signs on them, and the investigation that is made, and by the corrupt flesh that is over them.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary break is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone and rubs it gently, the break opens up black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a break, be careful about accidents that can occur in the patient. And if you see any bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, swelling, and fever ague, or if they persist and become red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot be healed with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a frightening accident and you hope for recovery, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound comes first to you, and it's in winter, then it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day of the moon that you can see.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the periosteum under the bone is not corrupted and the accidents we mentioned come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes right up to the cloth that covers the brain, then you must cut along the broken part thus; and take hold of the patient's head hurt, and uncover on the bone in all ways that you can, and above the appearance of the wound more gently than you can, and if a discharge of blood comes to uncover the bone, or a boil is formed, have recourse to what is needed, and make sure to fill the place with wet cloths in rose oil; and let the wound rest as long as the boil is calmed down, and be assured of the stopping of bleeding; then begin around the bone to take out, and it is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut on the thinning part before, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I put another tool, larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have a number of diverse tools, some narrow and others wide, and with a point, and made of iron. And work lightly, so as not to hurt the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and thick, you should pierce around it, so that you administer cuts with awls, not too deep lest they penetrate beyond the bone of the skull, and there must be above the tip a margin or 1 circle, so as to keep the tip from passing beyond the bone; and you will need several, each going in its place in the space of the bone, so that you have awls for all skulls; and this is the form of the 3 kinds of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you put one awl on top of the bone and turn back to your hands so long as you know the bone has been pierced; then place the awl elsewhere a little later, and thus do it all around, then cut with scissors the space of the bone which is between the piercings, and make it as thin as possible that you can, and lightly, as we have said, so that you bring out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as pliers, pincers; and be sure not to touch the brain or the spine.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and shaped the bone, then it is necessary that you reset the protruding part which remains of the bone to all other similar instruments resembling an incisor, but it must be sharper and more subtle than the other incisors; and if there remain any small bones or scales, then loosen them with instruments; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way of working is that which Galen says, who is more subtle, and his method is very strong, and it's his own word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	You must first uncover a part of the bone, at the place where the fracture is most apparent, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will put under the head of this lancet a lens-shaped thing:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is sharp in two sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then strike with a small mallet upwards, so that you lightly scratch the bone all around, and take good care of the membrane that is underneath; if it is attached to the bone, scratch it lightly, for we remove it without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture does not pierce up to the cloth, and the bone is chipped only on top, and there are small pieces, then you should scrape off that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine scraper which you should have various quantities of, so as to adjust in each place what is most convenient, according to the work and figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you pass before coarse scrapers, and then more fine ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other delicate cuts and subtle fractures, it is fitting that you adjust the cause according to its direction; and this is a thing that is not easy for one who has put their study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the scab is uncovered, you must take one cloth of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another double cloth of two or three layers, and soak it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do this as gently as possible, that you do not irritate the scab, then apply over the other bandage, but do not pull too tight until it touches only the wound; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscess is calmed down, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, and chickpea flour, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things; and make a powder of these things, and place it over the wound, and administer medicinal treatments without biting; and be careful that the wound is clean enough, that you do not leave ointment in it, nor assemble again with bowe, for when the bowe assembles itself on the cloth of the skin, they will corrode and rot, and cause great evil to the patient; for when you place over the scab something biting, it burns on top.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Be on guard then, if any bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackish humour does not come out as a result of the medicine that has been applied above, which should have such virtue, then you must take part of honey, and three parts of rose oil, and one drachm of aloes and smear it on; then treat him in the ways of cures that are necessary, until he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two bones above are broken, or one is broken alone, because they are two bones; and the one below is cartilaginous and does not break, unless it becomes twisted or turned, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you must push your little finger or a pointed instrument into the neck and insert the break even with the tip of your index finger, and through the back, until the neck returns to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your operation.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone and it cannot be set straight, then you should put a stick or a small rod into the head of the bone to support it.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, then do it similarly, and hasten to restore the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth, when the abscess has cooled down, then push a linen cloth through the head of the neck, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should bind another cloth on the other side, if it is there, and let them be so tight that they fill the holes of the bone.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And said a certain physician that one must wash the tents with lard, and move each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It doesn't seem right to me that it should be so, but they must be washed in a mixture of almond milk and egg white, and powder from the mill; then let the tent sit until the bone is hard and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes bind on or the bone some feathers of goose instead of bandages, and if it has a soft cloth wrapped around, and it holds the break in place, and the patient breathes easily through it; then do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if a swelling comes to the bone while you are working on it, then put a poultice of melted wax or cotton in rose oil, or in a small quantity of aquilantum (a type of ointment) onto it.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not come out, he puts a plaster on the outside, made from barley flour and incense powder, mixed with almond milk; then he puts on light bandages, and doesn't bind it too tight; and if the break in the arm is small, and it is broken into small pieces, he extracts it with suitable tools; then he sews up the crack, and cures things that seem to be charred flesh, and joining, such as plasters and ointments suitable for this; and if there is no wound inside the arm, he cures it with tents, and puts in poultices of plantain, until they are healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	It seems we've moved on to a new topic.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured below and there is no wound outside, and the breakage is only outward, and it is not split in two, but rather hollow inside, one recognizes this lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the breakage is in the right part, that you push your index finger into the patient's mouth; and if the breakage is on the left side of the jawbone, then push your index finger with the right hand and gently push the breakage inward, and secure it from the outside with the other hand, and tie equally.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jawbone fracture is split into two, it is necessary that you provide an extension of 1/2 part on each side, so that it becomes even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth are moved or broken, take hold of one end of a thread of gold or silver or silk, then place it on the fractured jawbone, and put on the jawbone a double cloth; and put on the cloth a large, well-made splint or a piece of leather equally long and wide as the jawbone, and tie it above your mouth, and command the patient to rest, and give him light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the patient's condition is changing for the worse, then take off the splint on the third day, and put back in place what had been changed; and apply ointment on it, made with flour mill powder mixed with egg or wheat flour, after taking out the cloth; and put on a light linen bandage. And if the ointment is hardened, and the patient's condition does not change for the worse, leave him be until he is healed; for many are healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if an abscess or swelling comes, administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, reward it with no part of the bone being extracted; if subtle from removing with suitable instruments to this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it with fire as needed according to your necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and none remain, close the wound, if it is wide, and put on one or two ointments suitable to this, to prevent pus, until they are healed.
de la forcele	of strength.
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forcelet (or deltoid muscle) breaks several times in front of the shoulder, and the break is according to three manners: or it is broken and disjointed in two, and there are pieces, and it is the easiest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the operation is thus when the break is without wound: that you have two assistants, one to hold the aid that feels the broken forcelet; and the other to extend the elbow towards the part; then place equally the break at your knees, so that the form be as it should be, and there be no appearance or wavering.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend further, put under the patient's shoulder an iron or rounded spear made of cloth or linen, and be as large as needed; then stretch and raise the forcelet, and grasp the spear with your hand, so that you place equally the break as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the forcelet out to the front because it comes in depth, it is necessary that the patient lies on their side over their bed, and puts a bolster under their shoulder; and pushes the assistant's shoulder down, so that the bone of the forcelet is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then align the break with your knees, and if you find that it is disjointed, it is necessary to split it apart; and pull out the light pieces, and if the bone cannot join together by any means, you cut off one of the parts with a knife that you have; but make sure to put this instrument under the forcelet, in order to prevent splintering.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it looks like a spoon and is not shaved and is just as large as it should be according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and has two joints, as you see, and one is wide and the other is narrow, as is the wound that you have made when you broke the bones; and when you are sure that there is a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the scabbing is small or you doubt a hot abscess, sew the wound with thread and tent cloth according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot inflammation comes, wet one cloth in rose oil, garlic, and vinegar, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	the immobilization of the bone, when it is not near wounds or incisions, is that you put powder made from mill dust and egg yolk on the bone, and put light compresses on top, and if necessary place a spear under the elbow; then take a very wide band, one palm in width, and put doubled cloth over the compresses and the plaster; then take a thin strip of three fingers in width and length, and envelop it around that bandage, so that the ends of the bandage are hanging down; and place the strip on the incision, and turn the bandage back over the shoulder and under the healthy elbow, and under the sick elbow; and tighten each part, and when you see that the dressing holds the arm well and you clearly see that the strip does not move above the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, restrain them; and make the patient lie on his back, and have him sleep with a small pillow under the elbow, to raise the shoulder high; thus it will relieve the fracture by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it if bad events come, until twenty days; then reapply the plaster if you see that it is necessary, and bind and leave it so, until it is restored; and it is restored in at most twenty-eight days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	The shoulder breaks or is severely out of place, and it cannot be known for sure until the touch; if it appears according to the shape of the break, and resets itself in its natural form, in all the ways that you can; then put powder from the mill on the joint with abundance of egg white, and light bandages, and double the cloth; then put a large and subtle splint, one pace more wide than the shoulder, and under the splint are nails in no place of the shoulder, so that the splintered hair of the linen bandage ties them equally; and then bind it with a great strong band tightly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and observe the ligature every day; and whenever it becomes loose, bind it again, and put the splint back in place if it gets out of place, and let the patient lie on their side; and the shoulder is restored in twenty days or twenty-five, And when this number is fulfilled, release it, and be sure, for it is not bone that will become loose suddenly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a part of the bone sticks out and points over the skin, then make a poultice on it, and apply an ointment, and do what we said to soothe a boil. (Note: The text is likely referring to a technique for managing a bone infection or abscess, where a poultice and ointment are used to draw out the infection.)
de la brisure dou pis	C'est le début de l'article ! "De la brisure du pis" est un titre qui suggère que l'article va traiter d'une blessure ou d'une rupture au sein (le "pis" désignant probablement le sein, mais peut aussi faire référence à une blessure à la poitrine).
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The bone is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downwards, and the patient feels great pain, has swelling, heat, and by chance vomits blood, and opens the sinews in the broken bone, and senses its presence.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back, and places a cushion between their shoulders, then presses the shoulders together, and aligns the ribs of the two broken ribs with their hands, and carefully adjusts it in all ways you can until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place plasters and bandages over the sharp point of salt or other light wood, and enclose it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone so that it does not move; and turn the string around to the back, and bind it tightly, and loosen it every hour for an air hole, and if it swells, tighten it again; and if it needs to be untied due to corrosion or itching that comes to the place, or pain or swelling, then hurry and untie it, and remove the plaster, and address what has come in ways of cures; then rinse the plaster, and bind it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Il semble que nous ayons une partie de l'ouvrage "La Chirurgie" d'Alphonse de Hautenville, un médecin du Moyen Âge.
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the breaking of the ribs does not occur except in thick places after the back, and at the top inside, and do not bend outwards except because they are slippery; and people sense this well through examination with their fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the remedy is that you place it evenly over the break, as it needs to be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then apply a poultice and tie with an iron band, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the breakage of the ribs is declining inside, the patient feels very great pain, and prickling, just like with pleurisy, because the bone pierces the membrane; and they vomit in needles, and are hot and throw up a large amount of blood, and this is a serious health issue, and the ancient people have put great remedies.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that it is necessary to administer foods that swell the belly, in order to drive the breakage outward.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, lest hot abscesses come to it, if they have not already come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, let them heal.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And one of us said that you put poultices on the spot, to draw out thoroughly, and this seems like reason; nevertheless, doubt exists that the poultice may attract unhealthy matter to the spot because of its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And one of us said that the spot should be covered with moist wool in hot oil, and you put tents between the ribs to put back in its place the hollow part around it, then take care of the treatment for pleurisy, meat, and medication.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot endure from the bone which pokes the cloth, and there is doubt in the patient, then you must cut open above the place of the broken rib, and put an instrument underneath to ward off the scab; and then you must saw through the bone, and draw it out lightly, and then sew together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with poultices until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, one should put moist cloths soaked in rose oil on it and place them on the affected area; and treat the surrounding area of the abscess as required for the abscess, and be vigilant that it does not spread to the adjacent side until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes the breakage of the bones of the neck occurs, and it makes them sag; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone and you want to know if they will be healed or not, look closely at whether you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and unable to move or stretch, and when you prick them with a needle, feel no sensation.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure. Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not happen to them, then the thing is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you bind it if there is a hot abscess, and put on a spine of rose oil or egg yolk oil as long as it is appeased; then put on one of the soothing and drying plasters, and tie it with a linen cloth, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where he feels pain, until he is healed.

And if any bone is separated, it must be covered with the knee; and remove the bone, then sew together the two edges of the wound, if they are large, with a seam; then treat it with ointment dripping fat, until he is healed; and if the ligament of the bone is broken, which is called the "ligament of the knee", take your left pouch and place it even with your right hand in your power, then put the plaster and iron on, if you need them; then bind it, and if there are separate bones, do that again, remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	The break of the bone of the hip.
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the bone of the hip is broken, then it will not be much diminished in value; and they do two long incisions, and cut towards the back, and come to the painful place, and puncture, and inflate what has been broken.

And the restoration is that you stretch out your hand over it, as long as you are above the breakage; and know what kind of break it is and its shape; and if the breakage is only in the head, place the breakage evenly, until it is back to its natural form.

de la brisure de l’ajutoire	The break of the arm.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The arm is what is between the shoulder and the head of the shoulder; and if it is broken, then it should be restored in one of two ways: one is that you take a wooden splint full of beeswax, with this shape...

And tie the two ends with two strips, and bend them upwards, and have the patient sit on a chair; then place their broken arm on the splint, so that it comes to the elbow, and put in the middle a wooden curve, then bend over some heavy thing or the attendants stretch it downwards; then apply the bandage to the breakage even with their hands together, until the breakage returns to its natural state.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie. And the manner of tying it is that you put the plaster on the breakage, then bring the arm onto the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put the bandage, and bind it on the shoulder and arm, so that the arm is in its natural state, unless something prevents it, or if the bone is moved.

And if you doubt that the bone is moved, then use splints, and put on the break a wider and stronger splint than the others, and have between each splint one piece of cloth, and let each splint be so large that it passes over the break three fingers from each side; then tie with the splints as I said at the beginning of this chapter on the breakage, but stronger and less distant.

And if you see the swelling of the stars and the strangulation, as we have said, in the part where you restore the broken member, and you doubt the warm abscess, let it stay at least until the seventh day, as we have said; then look every three days at the bandage, that itching or inflammation does not come to the place, or the discoloration cannot come to the member because it is too narrow.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it heals, as we have said.

de la brisure du bras	It looks like we've reached the end of the text about treating a broken arm.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", of which one is small, and that is the one that fits into the socket; and the other is large, and that is the one that is underneath, near the little joint; perhaps only break the large foscile, or the small, and perhaps both together.
